Current Affairs Commentary

Twists and Turns in the Franco-Soviet Agreement

— Heng

Since the rapprochement between France and the Soviet Union last spring, the representatives of both countries have done their utmost to act in concert on the international stage. As a result, the two countries first proposed the Eastern European Pact and then France introduced Soviet Russia to join the League of Nations. Subsequently, there have been frequent rumors of a military alliance between France and the Soviet Union. From a superficial observation, it seems that the diplomatic relations between the two countries are harmonious and without any differences. However, only after the recent exposure of the draft of the Franco-Soviet Agreement did it become clear that the close relationship between France and the Soviet Union over the past year is indeed a fact, but there seem to be still issues regarding the conclusion of a military alliance of offense and defense. France wants to conclude an agreement with Russia within the framework of the League of Nations, while the Soviet Union expects an automatic mutual assistance pact. The former is modeled after the Locarno Pact in Western Europe, and the latter is similar to the pre-war offensive and defensive alliance. According to a European dispatch on the 20th, Litvinov abruptly ended his trip to Paris because France could not accept his proposal for automatic mutual assistance. From this, it can be seen that although the friendship between France and the Soviet Union has been more than a year, their wills and expectations have not yet been consistent.

There are three reasons why France and the Soviet Union want to conclude this agreement. First, they fear that Germany has no intention of concluding the Eastern European Pact, so they want to replace the effect of the Eastern European Pact with this agreement. Second, they want to use this to pressure Germany to accept the Eastern European Pact. Third, if Germany can join the Eastern European Pact, then this agreement can be used as a supplementary pact to the Eastern European Pact. When the Western European Locarno Pact was concluded in 1925, France separately concluded similar agreements with Poland and Czechoslovakia to assist the function of the Locarno Pact. The current Franco-Soviet Agreement is nothing more than an attempt to conclude it in advance, thereby pressuring Germany to comply. According to a Geneva dispatch on the 9th, the content of the draft Franco-Soviet Agreement is largely based on the Charter of the League of Nations. The nature of this agreement is purely similar to the Western European Locarno Pact and even more similar to the Franco-Polish and Franco-Czech treaties assisting the Locarno Pact. In a word, the function of these treaties is nothing more than seeking the application of League of Nations sanctions within the scope of the League of Nations, which is quite different from the pre-war offensive and defensive alliance. The difference between them can be understood by simply examining the provisions in the Locarno Pact. According to the provisions of Article 4 of the Pact, if one of the contracting states believes that the other party has committed an act of aggression, it shall report the facts to the Council of the League of Nations. Only after the Council has verified the facts can it immediately notify the contracting states to assist the invaded party. This is significantly different from the automatic mutual assistance of an offensive and defensive alliance. The reason for such a provision is nothing more than to decide the responsibility of right and wrong by the League of Nations, so as not to allow warmongers to take advantage of it. However, when the Council of the League of Nations cannot unanimously accept the report, each country has the right to take free action out of the necessity of maintaining justice and fairness (see Article 2 of the Locarno Pact and Article 1 of the Franco-Polish and Franco-Czech treaties). The caution of the procedures regarding free action can be seen from this. Therefore, the function of the Locarno Treaty is not only to guarantee the security of France, but also to prevent France from freely invading Germany. The reason why Britain was willing to guarantee this treaty at that time was because this treaty had this spirit of maintaining peace. If the agreement that France wants to conclude with the Soviet Union wants to obtain Britain's support, it will inevitably not be able to surpass the precedent of the Locarno Treaty. Otherwise, gaining one Soviet Union and losing one Britain would not be worthwhile for France.

However, the Soviet Union seems to be focusing on the agility of military action and does not want to wait for the decision of a third party, which may delay the temporary military opportunity. Therefore, it advocates automatic mutual assistance and does not take the League of Nations as its main body. If this kind of treaty can be established, its power to restrain Germany will naturally be stronger than that of the Locarno-style treaty. However, judging from the situation in Eastern Europe, the Soviet Union is now suspected by Poland. If the Franco-Soviet Agreement is indeed the same as the previous offensive and defensive alliance, Poland will feel uneasy. At present, France is trying to befriend Poland. This is also one of the reasons why France insists on taking the League of Nations as the main body for the Franco-Soviet Agreement. Although, if the Soviet Union aims at self-defense and also takes into account France's wishes, then the Franco-Soviet Agreement, despite many twists and turns, will eventually have the possibility of mutual conclusion.

Major Earthquake in Taiwan: Death Toll Exceeds 3,000; Serious and Minor Injuries Reach Over 8,000; Aftershocks Continue; Relief Efforts are Busy; Earthquake Center is the Daan River Between Hsinchu and Taichung

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Colonial Affairs received a report on the damage situation of the Taiwan earthquake at 7:00 PM on the 22nd, as follows: Deaths: 3,003; Serious injuries: 7,216; Minor injuries: 845; Total deaths and injuries: 11,664; Totally collapsed houses: 11,780; Half-collapsed houses: 11,731; Heavily damaged: 2,805; Slightly damaged: 1,823; Total collapsed and damaged houses: 28,139. The actual situation in the disaster area is gradually increasing as continuous investigations are conducted, and it is extremely tragic. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

Taipei As of 9:00 PM on the 21st, the number of confirmed deaths has exceeded 2,700, the number of injured is 9,000, and the number of victims has reached hundreds of thousands. The affected areas are far from the city and in places with inconvenient transportation, so relief work cannot proceed smoothly, and aftershocks continue. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) According to the announcement of the Central Meteorological Observatory, the center of the major earthquake in Taiwan is located in the lower reaches of the Daan River on the border between Hsinchu Prefecture and Taichung Prefecture. The depth of the epicenter is still shallow, about 10 kilometers or less from the surface, so the ground shaking is extremely intense locally. There may still be considerable aftershocks in the future, but they will gradually subside. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

Taipei According to the investigation of the Taiwan government, the major earthquake in Taichung Prefecture is the most intense since the Chiayi earthquake in 1906. At that time, the number of deaths was 1,300, and the casualties this time are several times that number. (22nd Hua-lien Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The loss from this major earthquake in Taiwan is indeed an unprecedented disaster on the island. The total number of collapsed houses is about 20,000, and the damage is about 6 million yuan. In addition, the damage to bridges and other various losses is also about 4 million yuan. The total amount of damage is about 10 million yuan. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

Taichung A reporter from the Japan Associated Press took a car to the earthquake zone last night to inspect the state of the disaster. Residents of Zhunan were taking refuge on the roadside or in open spaces, and the sound of wailing did not stop. There were many cracks in the ground, the larger ones being more than six feet and the smaller ones being three or four feet. Traffic was dangerous, and the authorities posted notices everywhere prohibiting passage. The villages along the road were almost completely destroyed. The tragic situation in the epicenter of the Daan River was unbearable to witness. Rumors abounded in Fengyuan and Dajia, and many were arrested by the authorities. The military, police officers, and youth groups were fully mobilized to transport food, sanitary materials, etc. Aftershocks have repeatedly struck here, and we have not yet escaped the dangerous situation. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

Taichung and Hsinchu Disaster Statistics

Taipei According to the announcement of the Taiwan Governor-General's Police Bureau, the damage situation confirmed as of 8:00 PM on the 21st is as follows:

Fengyuan County, Taichung Prefecture

Deaths: 1,270, Serious injuries: 3,738

Totally collapsed houses: 1,201, Half-collapsed: 312

Dajia County

Deaths: 314, Serious injuries: 460, Totally collapsed: 909, Half-collapsed: 342

Dongshi County

Deaths: 31, Serious injuries: 85

Totally collapsed: 354, Half-collapsed: 434 In addition to other damage, the total damage in the prefecture is 1,617 deaths, 4,296 injuries, 2,485 totally collapsed houses, and 446 half-collapsed houses.

Miaoli County, Hsinchu Prefecture

Deaths: 468, Injuries: 590

Totally collapsed: 1,057, Half-collapsed: 1,249

Zhunan County

Deaths: 205, Injuries: 131

Totally collapsed: 2,394, Half-collapsed: 768

Dahu County

Deaths: 164, Injuries: 241

Totally collapsed: 242, Half-collapsed: 108

Zhudong County

Deaths: 13, Injuries: 94

Totally collapsed: 416, Half-collapsed: 694

Hsinchu City

Deaths: 414, Injuries: 58

Totally collapsed: 129

Including other damage in the prefecture, the total damage is 854 deaths, 971 injuries, 4,186 totally collapsed houses, and 4,586 half-collapsed houses. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

Taipei In Neipu Village, which suffered extremely heavy damage, all the houses were destroyed, and the village head, assistant, principals of public and private schools, and many other influential people were crushed to death. The surviving villagers, having lost their leaders, barely escaped with their lives and fled empty-handed, with many unable to get up due to hunger. In the Tunzi Jiao village of Neipu, as of noon on the 21st, more than 500 bodies had been found. The entire village was wiped out, and the situation was extremely tragic. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

Taipei Although the damage in Taichung Prefecture is great, the damage in Taichung City is minimal. The refugees moving into Taichung from the south are in a wartime state. The injured from Neipu Village, Shengang Village, and Houhe Li are continuously being transported to Taichung by trucks, cars, and handcarts. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

Condolences from Various Countries

(Tokyo) Ambassadors and ministers from various countries stationed in Japan visited Foreign Minister Hirota today to express their condolences for the Taiwan earthquake. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

(Washington) The chairman of the American Red Cross, Mr. Clayson, heard about the Taiwan earthquake and stated that the American Red Cross is willing to do its best to help the disaster and reduce the suffering of the disaster victims in Taiwan. (20th Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Hong Kong naval authorities have stated that they are willing to assist in the relief of the earthquake that occurred in Taiwan yesterday to the best of their ability and are actively preparing. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(London) It is reported that the British government has proposed to Japan to send ships stationed in China to carry food and medical supplies to rescue the disaster victims in Taiwan. If Japan accepts this request, several British ships currently in Hong Kong can be prepared to depart. Admiral Dreyer, commander of the British fleet in China, is currently in Japan and is reportedly in contact with the Japanese authorities in Tokyo regarding all matters. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

Active Relief Efforts

(Tokyo) Colonial Minister Kodama visited Foreign Minister Okada this afternoon to report on the Taiwan earthquake situation and discuss relief matters. After that, he went to the Imperial Palace to meet the Emperor and reported everything. All officials of the Ministry of Colonial Affairs decided to donate 1% of their salaries and send them to the disaster area urgently. The Ministry of Home Affairs issued an order to the governors of all prefectures to raise donations. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Colonial Affairs is currently planning to compile detailed reports from the disaster area, establish a post-earthquake disaster countermeasures committee within the ministry, and coordinate with various parties before starting activities. It is also planning to use this earthquake disaster as an opportunity to promote the integration of Taiwanese people and Japanese mainlanders. Regarding the rescue of refugees and the restoration of the disaster area, it should be done without regret to ensure perfection. It was also instructed by the Emperor to actively strive for the integration of mainlanders and Taiwanese people, and the outline for its realization has been decided. Colonial Minister Kodama has already sent a telegram to Taiwan Governor-General Nakagawa with the above intentions. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) According to the report of the Taiwan Governor-General's Office to the Ministry of Colonial Affairs, the weather in the earthquake-stricken area is very good today, and various relief efforts are proceeding smoothly. People's hearts have been stabilized. This earthquake has hardly affected the indigenous people's areas. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

Taipei The rescue team of the 1st Taipei Regiment rode in cars to Zhunan on the evening of the 21st and distributed bread and other food all night. However, the areas with the most severe damage lack food, and they have requested the prefectural authorities to continue to issue food. The garrisons in Taipei and Tainan are taking a standby posture in case of emergency. There is no chaos at present, and only military police officers are maintaining order. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

Taipei The damage in Taichung City is relatively light, with very few houses collapsing. All Japanese houses are fine, and only Taiwanese houses made of earth have suffered more damage. The Governor-General's Office has organized three relief teams, which traveled by train from Taipei on the afternoon of the 21st to provide relief. The Military Command has also sent a relief team. There may even be a need to dispatch troops to guard the earthquake-stricken area. At 1:00 PM yesterday, standby orders were issued to the troops in the city, as in the case of the Great Kanto Earthquake, the earthquake was followed by fire, and the damage from the fire was extremely tragic. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Finance is planning to compile a detailed report on the major earthquake in Taiwan and then immediately convene a meeting of executives. It is reported that the decided policy is roughly as follows: 1. A total of 7.4 million yuan, including 1.7 million yuan from the special accounting second reserve fund for Taiwan and 5.7 million yuan from the surplus of the special accounting item, can be proposed for use in order to discuss emergency relief measures. 2. Investigate the degree of damage according to the inland earthquake disaster as a standard and decide to reduce or exempt income tax, business income tax, inheritance tax, etc. to show consideration.

3. Investigate the state of damage. If it is deemed necessary for recovery and reconstruction, the deposit department will provide low-interest funds. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) All parts of the country have already sympathized with the relief efforts for the Taiwan earthquake. First, the Ministry of Home Affairs and the Ministry of Colonial Affairs negotiated and planned to work with local government offices throughout the country to start raising donations. Now the Tokyo Municipal Government has decided to raise funds for disaster relief. The Ministry of Colonial Affairs is implementing a plan for all employees to withdraw 1% of their monthly salaries as voluntary donations. The Ministry of Railways has now negotiated with the Postal Steamship and Osaka Shosen companies to offer discounts or free shipping for all relief supplies to Taiwan. The Red Cross Society has convened an emergency board meeting to organize a rescue team and send it to the disaster area to provide services. The Special Volunteer Nurse Association has also started to handle relief work separately. Other organizations such as the Patriotic Women's Association, the Salvation Army, the Higashi Honganji Temple, and other social welfare groups, whether public or private, have all risen to carry out relief efforts and have started donation campaigns separately. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

Impact on the Sugar Industry

Taichung The Japan Oil Company, which has a kerosene mine in Miaoli County, Hsinchu Prefecture, in the earthquake epicenter, and the Kinsui Mine and Daibinhon in Zhunan County, is investigating the damage situation. Only part of the building collapsed in the former, and only the gas line was cut off in the latter. There were no casualties. Also, regarding the damage to sugar, since the center of the damage is Taichung Prefecture and the northern part of Hsinchu Prefecture, rather than the central sugar-producing area, the impact on the sugar industry is relatively minor. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

Taichung The most severely damaged Dajia Street and Shimizu Street are famous producing areas of Panama hats, and Panama hats are currently being manufactured, so the impact on the supply and demand of Panama hats is very large. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

Exchange of Ambassadors Between China and Turkey: Minister He to Arrive Soon; Embassy Already Prepared

Turkish Capital China and Turkey recently concluded a treaty of friendship and exchanged ambassadors. The newly appointed Chinese minister to Turkey, He Yaozu, set sail to Turkey some days ago. The staff of the embassy, led by the first secretary Wang Wan-sheng, came here some days ago to prepare everything. Wang is a famous historian, who recently gave a speech to reporters here, stating that China and Turkey have had a long and close friendly relationship since the eleventh century BC. Wang also said that he has brought some ancient Chinese books, which can prove that the relationship between China and Turkey has not been interrupted since ancient times, which is sufficient to ensure the current friendship between China and Turkey. It is reported that after Chinese minister He Yaozu arrives here, the two countries will begin negotiations and conclude a commercial treaty. (22nd Havas Dispatch)

Minister Arima Arrives in Japan

(Tokyo) Minister Arima stationed in China, accompanied by his wife and Secretary Yano, arrived in Kobe at 9:04 this morning on the Tatsuta Maru and then took a train to Tokyo. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

(Shimonoseki) Colonel Sakai, Chief of Staff of the Chinese Garrison Army, arrived here today on the Baikal Maru to attend the Tokyo Chiefs of Staff Conference and took the 9:50 AM train to Tokyo. (22nd Den-tsu Dispatch)

Two Japanese Naval Aircraft Conduct Drills Across the Sea of Japan, Departing from Saeki and Flying to Najin Yesterday Morning

Nagasaki Two flying boats belonging to the Saeki Naval Air Group, commanded by Colonel Arisawa, flew to Najin, Korea this morning at 9:00 AM, will fly to Ominato tomorrow, and will fly back the day after tomorrow, to conduct drills in the Sea of Japan area. (22nd Hua-lien Dispatch)

Cabinet Establishment of Deliberation Council Issue: Four Elders Hold Meeting

(Tokyo) Prime Minister Okada convened a meeting of the Four Elders at his official residence at 11:30 this morning. Finance Minister Takahashi, Communications Minister Tokonami, and Commerce Minister Machida attended. Minister of State Yoshida was specially ordered to participate. They deliberated on the members of the Cabinet Deliberation Council and countermeasures for the current situation. Yoshida reported on his meeting with Nagata, Director of the Military Affairs Bureau, this morning, and then began deliberation. They adjourned after lunch. It is reported that the biggest difficulties at present are (1) the issue of the Seiyukai's participation and (2) the military's opinion on the Deliberation Council. (22nd Hua-lien Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Nagata, Director of the Military Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of the Army, visited Cabinet Secretary-General Yoshida on the morning of the 22nd. After listening to the government's detailed intentions regarding the Cabinet Deliberation Council issue, he explained the army's views as follows: (1) The Cabinet Deliberation Council is to select authoritative functional representatives from all parties to investigate and study the major national policies of the current extraordinary situation. It is also a very significant organization, which is what we expect. (2) Therefore, the selection of its members should be authoritative functional representatives from all parties and be knowledgeable and capable people. If it is used to assist the work of the Cabinet, it is absolutely opposed, and it is decided that the members of the Deliberation Council must also deliberate, study, and formulate plans for the Investigation Bureau in the future, and exercise endorsement. Therefore, there is no need to decide on any members in advance. The appointment of the Director of the Investigation Bureau, who handles actual affairs, should be valued. (3) Regarding the operation of the Deliberation Council, the army is doing its best to avoid recognizing it as an auxiliary organ of the Cabinet. Therefore, in principle, the Deliberation Council should remove matters related to the budget for the next year, because it should be considered as an organ that actually decides national policies for a long period of two or three years in the future. (22nd Japan Associated Press Dispatch)

New England Textile Industry Declines Sharply: Fifteen Factories Close; Over Ten Thousand Workers Unemployed

Boston According to a survey by a certain party, the textile industry in the New England region is currently facing extremely difficult conditions. Fifteen major textile factories have closed this year, resulting in the unemployment of 12,000 workers. It is likely that several of them will not reopen. In addition, the factories that are still in operation have had to reduce their output. It is said that this situation is due to the government's collection of cotton production business tax and is not due to competition from Japanese goods. Therefore, manufacturers believe that the tax must be abolished before the textile industry can be hoped to recover. (22nd Kuomintang News Agency Dispatch)

Japan Plans to Develop the Southeast European Market: Provides Bulgarian Merchant Ships for a Far East Mobile Exhibition; Requests Sofia as a Hub for Promoting Trade

(London) Japan is now providing a 19,000-ton merchant ship for the Bulgarian government to hold a mobile exhibition of Bulgarian goods in the Far East. According to a telegram from Sofia today, the Japanese government stated that it is prepared to increase Bulgaria's trade with Japan and Manchuria, but Bulgaria must allow Japan to establish a Japanese goods promotion agency in Sofia as a hub for Japan to promote its trade in the Southeast European market. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

Regional Mutual Assistance Pact: Franco-Soviet Negotiations Suddenly Encounter Obstacles; Differences of Opinion Still Exist; Litvinov Returns Home to Report; France Does Not Want to Conflict with Obligations Under the Locarno Pact; Russia Insists on Having the Freedom to Use Force

(Paris) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a statement saying that negotiations on the conclusion of a mutual assistance treaty between France and the Soviet Union have been temporarily suspended. Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov originally planned to come here to sign the first word on the treaty, but was temporarily recalled to Moscow by the Russian government to report to the People's Committee on the negotiations with French Foreign Minister Laval. The French Ministry of Foreign Affairs did not explain why the setback occurred. Many believe that it is because France wants the treaty to be established within the framework of the League of Nations and not to hinder France's obligations under the Locarno Pact, while Russia clearly wants the mutual assistance clauses to be automatic. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

(Paris) According to a statement released by TASS, "Negotiations between Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov and French Foreign Minister Laval on the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact have been temporarily suspended. Mr. Litvinov has been summoned back to the country to report on the progress of the negotiations to the Soviet People's Committee." Regarding the temporary suspension of negotiations mentioned in the statement, we should know that Litvinov's negotiations could not continue as he traveled from Geneva to Moscow. As for Mr. Litvinov's intention to report on the difficulties in drafting the text of the Mutual Assistance Pact to the government, this is also a matter of course. (21st Havas Dispatch)

(Paris) The French press is paying close attention to the issue of Franco-Soviet cooperation. Le Siècle said that this cooperation has been felt in previous diplomatic negotiations, especially at the Stresa Conference and in Geneva. It is rumored in Geneva that the Franco-Soviet agreement will be signed soon, and we cannot deny the great impact of this statement. The newspaper continued, "France's efforts to conclude the Franco-Soviet Pact as soon as possible are precisely because the governments of some European countries are trying to undermine this pact." Le Petit Journal sought the opinions of French politicians on the Franco-Soviet Pact. Former Prime Minister Pangou responded, "I believe that if the Regional Mutual Assistance Pact is concluded within the scope of the League of Nations, it will strengthen the effect of obligations." Senator Sarraut expressed his welcome to the formal confirmation of Franco-Soviet friendship. Former Education Minister Anatole said that France wants peace, and so does the Soviet Union. Therefore, if the Soviet Union and France can work together, there will be results. He said that this treaty is by no means a military alliance against any country, but a new guarantee for us and the pacification of the world. (21st TASS Dispatch)

Parisian Newspaper Reveals Secret German-Polish Agreement with Military Mutual Assistance Clause, Valid for Two Years

(Moscow) It is rumored that a secret agreement exists between Germany and Poland, containing clauses for military mutual assistance in case of aggression. Soviet Russian newspapers published this major news yesterday, reprinting it from a provincial French newspaper. The original article was signed by Raimu, a former French cabinet member. Soviet Russian newspapers published the article without criticism, while officials here neither confirmed nor denied it, remaining silent. It is said that the agreement was concluded on February 25th. (National Telegram, 21st)

(Paris) Germany and Poland signed a ten-year non-aggression pact on January 26th of last year, which improved their mutual relations. Subsequently, another agreement was concluded but has not been made public. According to the "National Welfare Newspaper" of Lyon, which published the full text obtained from former Commerce Minister Raimu, the contents are divided into eight articles. The "Parisian Echo" newspaper especially carried the following: (1) The contracting countries agree to consult each other directly and cooperate effectively on any international issues affecting them. (2) Poland agrees that all its diplomatic decisions shall conform to Germany's opinions and shall safeguard Germany's interests. (3) The contracting countries agree that if any international events occur that threaten the status quo, they shall immediately notify each other and reach mutual understanding to take beneficial measures. (4) The contracting countries agree that if one of the parties is attacked by a third country without provocation, they shall immediately resist jointly with their respective military, economic, and financial power. (5) Poland agrees that if Germany's eastern and northeastern neighbors provoke Germany, it shall allow German troops to pass freely through Polish territory. (6) Germany agrees to guarantee Poland's current borders. (7) The contracting countries agree to take all economic measures within the scope of common interests, especially economic measures sufficient to consolidate the defense matters of each country. (8) This agreement shall be valid for two years. Unless one of the contracting countries declares its termination six months in advance, it shall be automatically extended. Within the two-year term of this agreement, each contracting country may declare its termination six months in advance. (Havas Telegram, 22nd)

Germans Emphasize Geneva Resolution, Maintaining Honor by Relying on Strength, Public Opinion Supports Government Policy

(Berlin) Berlin newspapers commented on the government's protest against the League of Nations Administrative Council's adoption of the French proposal condemning Germany's reintroduction of compulsory military service. They all stated that Germany's withdrawal from the League of Nations was justified. The "Germania Newspaper" stated that the implementation of compulsory military service could no longer be delayed for Germany's political calculations. The "Berlin Daily News" stated that the German government takes the resolution passed in Geneva very seriously. The "Local News" stated that the powers should recognize that Germany's protest merely expresses the thinking of all the German people. (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

(Berlin) All German newspapers unanimously support the German government's formal protest against the League of Nations resolution of April 17th, narrating the historical oppression suffered from foreign countries that forced Germany to seek its own survival. The "Berlin Daily News" stated that when the German government announced the implementation of conscription on March 16th, it solemnly declared that limiting the German army to twelve army corps aimed to quell the slanderous talk of Germany intending to dominate. This number does not encompass all the able-bodied men in Germany eligible for military service. The other purpose of this resolution is to proclaim to the German and other peoples that Germany will henceforth maintain its honor and security by relying on its own strength. The content of the German note is also the same. Not long ago, the countries expressed willingness to gradually abolish the military provisions in the Treaty of Versailles. This was not done out of intimidation but because they recognized that the perpetual existence of that treaty would have only harmful consequences. However, this hope was never realized, so Germany ultimately had no choice but to seek its own survival. (National Telegram, 21st)

Commemorating Revolutionary Martyrs, Southern Ireland Passes Peacefully, Republican Army Parades, Avoiding Conflicts With Government Troops

After the speech, he quietly withdrew without interference. The head of the Irish Free State, Fannella, also gave a speech to the public at the post office, the center of the 1916 uprising, and received the salute of 7,000 Free State troops at that place. The troops marched past him in formation, which lasted two hours. Fannella had previously held a ceremony to unveil a monument to the fallen in the uprising. The monument was moved to a safe place by the Irish Republican Army because of their resentment of the government's recent arrests of party members, and was closely guarded all day. Fannella expressed his desire for the early establishment of the Irish Republic, but he felt that the time had not yet come to implement this. The Irish Republican Army also paraded, but far less vigorously than the Free State troops. The Irish Republican Army staggered to the cemetery in heavy rain and did not hold any ceremonies. The day passed peacefully without any incidents, and the people were relieved. Previously, the government troops and the Irish Republican Army were stationed in Dublin and its surrounding areas, preparing to stage demonstrations to commemorate the martyrs of the 1916 uprising. The two armies were facing each other, and the people were worried that the two sides might inevitably clash. Although the Irish Republican Army has recently been declared an illegal organization by the government, the authorities still allowed them to parade, but Woconnell Street, the site of the 1916 uprising, was not allowed to be passed through. Fortunately, they detoured and did not try to force their way through, so a conflict was avoided. (Reuters Telegram, 21st)

Details of Jesus' Passion, Accuracy of Biblical Account Proven by Anatomical Research

(Paris) The account of Jesus' crucifixion in the Bible has recently been supported by anatomical evidence. According to the account, Jesus suffered five wounds during his passion: his hands and feet were pierced by nails, and his heart was pierced by a spear. When the body was removed from the cross, blood stains seeped into the shroud, which is clearly discernible. This shroud is currently kept in Turin, Italy. Dr. Barbet, a surgeon at Saint Joseph's Hospital in Paris, recently studied the five wounds from an anatomical perspective and conducted real-world tests on the corpse. The results matched the blood stains on the shroud. Barbet thus concluded that the account of Jesus' execution in the Bible is completely accurate. (Havas Telegram, 21st)

Northwest Inspection Notes

— Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

The Great Buddha Temple and Zuo Gong's Willow Trees

Leaving Changwu eastward, the car initially went along the south of the city. The city walls were trenched to form moats, naturally deep and dangerous. After twenty *li*, we arrived at Ranjia Shop. The villagers live in caves, with deep pits dug into the ground, about three to four *zhang* square. On each of the three walls, caves are carved for living or storing grain. The remaining walls are only pierced with tunnels, serving as doorways, either leading up to the ground or connecting horizontally to the four directions. Cattle and horses can also enter and exit freely. The bottom of the square pit serves as a courtyard, suitable for threshing wheat. Some pits even have surrounding walls. Poor families simply carve caves into the edge of a cliff, build walls and set up doors, and they can live there. After twenty-five *li*, we reached Tingkou, a small town located between Changwu and Bin counties, where a market is held. The road had already descended from the plateau and followed the banks of the Jing River. The fertile fields were either planted with wheat or poppies, all of which had sprouted green shoots. According to the farmers, one *mu* of poppies can yield twenty *liang* of opium, which can be sold for ten foreign dollars, just enough to cover the *mu* tax. In reality, there is no surplus profit to be made.

Entering Xie County to the east, formerly the ancient Yong 　State, is a strategic high ground. Newly built blockhouses, with their high and sturdy design, are quite convenient for watchmen. After twenty *li*, we arrived at the Great Buddha Temple, where a large Buddha is carved into a rock cave, with a single-faced hall built outside. The Buddha is seven or eight *zhang* tall, solemn and magnificent. Entering the temple to view it, one truly feels the awe of looking up to immense height. There are also many other large and small Buddha caves. All the engineering techniques are similar to those of the Buddhist caves in Datong and Dunhuang. This temple is the Qingshou Temple of the Tang Dynasty, supervised by Yuchi Jingde, also a major historical project. From here, jujube and pear orchards are abundant. After fifteen *li*, we arrived at Huaguo Mountain, where the Water Curtain Cave is also located. The cliffs and caves are dangerous and strange, and the scenery is beautiful and secluded. Climbing and sightseeing are accompanied by numerous legends. After ten *li*, we entered Bin City. The city is rectangular, with the Bin Mountain to the south and the Jing River to the north. The western part is desolate, while the eastern part is prosperous. A tall pagoda stands in the center, visible from afar. Pears, jujubes, and honey have long been famous products. The pears have yellow skin, thick stems, and are indeed incomparably fragrant and delicious. However, after careful tasting, they are still inferior to the Snowflake Pears of Ding County. We happened to see the local militia from the four villages, each carrying spears, coming to the city for inspection. They wore blue cloth round hats, with cotton wads wrapped on top like fists, and walked with a bobbing and swaying gait, no different from those worn by the clownish family servants in Peking opera. It seems to be a continuation of ancient styles, which is quite interesting to watch.

Leaving the city for three or four *li*, we ascended to the plateau again. Descending the winding road, we saw people living in caves, truly a case of "carriages and horses still pass over the rooftops." By the time we reached Yongshou County, the two cities were only seventy *li* apart. Yong City stands alone on a hillside, with a very small population, and has been repeatedly captured by bandits. The county government has been temporarily relocated to other towns. After forty *li*, we reached Jianjun Ba. There are still many residents. The road is low and sunken by eight or nine *chi*. The store doors and steps face each other like high banks. The market runs between the two sides, with carriages and horses traveling in the middle. Although the layout is old, it avoids congestion. Afterwards, we traveled on a flat plain for sixty or seventy *li*, sloping slightly downwards. The car traveled very quickly, heading straight to the north gate of Qian County. The terrain was still sloping. The sun had already set in the west, so we stayed at an inn. Many areas in the city are also desolate. The bustling areas are only in one part. The market people were dispersing, and the noise was chaotic. Beggars went from house to house asking for money, knocking on bamboo clappers and singing Qin腔 opera. Each household had a different tune, craning their necks and stamping their feet, their demeanor just like on a stage. The shopkeeper threw coppers early, and the beggar would definitely finish singing the last sentence of the opera according to the tune before bowing to pick them up and leaving leisurely. Are these also opera fans?

The "Zuo Gong's Willow Trees" planted on both sides of the Shaanxi-Gansu post road, during their prosperous period, stretched from Tongguan in the east to Jiayuguan in the west, for a total of thirty to forty *li*. Their high branches shaded the sun, and their thick foliage covered the road. Travelers on the road, enjoying the shade, all praised the legacy of Zuo. It is not easy to advocate planting trees, and it is even more difficult to grow trees into forests. To form a forest with historical value, national defense, and transportation significance is especially commendable. Unfortunately, the government offices in the counties along the willow line do not know how to protect them, and they allow unruly people to wantonly destroy them, either peeling the bark in search of insects under the pretext of treating diseases, or claiming that they were broken by wind and rain, stealing and felling them for firewood, resulting in broken stretches, no longer as prosperous as before. Especially on the post roads we passed in the past two days, often traveling for dozens of *li* without a single tree, the desolation is overwhelming, truly letting down the predecessors.

The uses of forests are extremely extensive. In terms of industrial needs, in addition to construction, they can be used to make various paper materials, rayon, medicines, photographic films, paints, alcohol, and smokeless gunpowder. Among all countries, only the Soviet Union, Canada, and Poland can be self-sufficient in forest products. Our country, however, mostly relies on imports. Every year, timber imports average 30 million yuan, which is indeed a major drain. Although the Northwest has a vast area, it is mostly barren mountains and wilderness, left to waste, abandoning resources in the ground. We already feel the lack of production and suffer from droughts and floods. If we can cultivate forests on this land, we can immediately create a source of wealth. Moreover, the climate of the Northwest is continental and desert-like. When the north wind rises, dust and sand cover the sky. The idea that deserts are migrating south is not unfounded. If we do not actively afforest, the future is truly worrying. The benefits of afforestation, such as planting pines and firs, can yield more than eight times the profit after twelve years. Planting tung trees yields fruit in three years and abundant harvests in five years. By the eighth or ninth year, each tree can yield an average profit of seven or eight yuan. If you plant one thousand two hundred trees, you can earn one ten thousand yuan in profit every year. The cost is small and the profit is large, which is unmatched by other trees. In particular, Shaanxi Province, known for its tung oil, should vigorously promote planting. As for the indirect benefits of afforestation, such as regulating the climate, conserving water sources, preventing droughts and floods, sheltering against wind and sand, enhancing scenery, and benefiting sanitation, they are too numerous to mention. The French scholar Cortelbert once said, "What destroys France is not foreign enemies, but the devastation of its mountains and forests." This statement is no different from prescribing acupuncture for our Northwest. In the future, we should plant new trees extensively and protect old forests, and we should take both approaches simultaneously, without further delay.

The Current State of Northern Manchurian Soybeans Under Japanese and Puppet Manipulation: The Japanese and Puppet Authorities Buy Soybeans at Low Prices for Profit; Anticipating Reduced Sales, They Will Restrict Planting

Harbin Correspondence: Northern Manchurian soybeans occupy an important position in the world market. Since July of last year, when Germany temporarily banned the import of oilseed raw materials, the export of Northern Manchurian soybeans has been severely hit, and the price per *pu* dropped to around five *jiao*. The puppet Ministry of Industry, seeing the potential for profit, implemented manipulation and organized the Daxing Company to buy soybeans at low prices. Last year, Northeast China suffered from severe floods, and the soybean harvest in the flooded areas was greatly reduced, accounting for only one-third of previous years. The oilseed raw materials such as rapeseed and flaxseed in Western European countries also had poor harvests. Later, Germany resumed soybean imports due to its commercial treaty with Japan. At the same time, the Japanese and puppet authorities vigorously sought to sell soybeans to various parts of South China. As a result, soybean exports showed signs of recovery. The Japanese and puppet authorities made heavy profits in the process, and the soybean market price rose from five *jiao* to six *jiao*. During this period, the market price was temporarily stable for a while. Soon, as soybean stocks decreased day by day, speculators rushed to buy, and the market gradually increased. On February 21 of this year, the price of soybeans rose to one yuan, three *jiao*, six *fen*, five *li* per *pu*, the highest soybean price in recent years. Before long, it gradually decreased again. At present, it is one yuan, one *jiao*, six *fen*, which is still not lower than the price of seven or eight *jiao* per *pu* in December last year. Many people with stocks are waiting and watching and not selling. However, the Japanese and puppet authorities want to implement export manipulation, so they say that Western European countries have planted more rapeseed and flaxseed and other oilseeds to resist soybean imports. Japan is also using chemical methods to manufacture various fertilizers to replace the purchase of bean cakes and other things. It is predicted that soybean exports are not optimistic. Therefore, they have set a restriction plan. Those in Southern Manchuria who plant more miscellaneous grains will plant more cotton in the future. Those in Northern Manchuria who plant more soybeans will plant more wheat in the future to limit soybean production and promote exports to lower market prices. As for the wheat production in Northeast China, the annual output is often not enough for local use, and imports are more than exports. Therefore, it is also possible to restrict the planting of more wheat. At the same time, the puppet authorities are studying the promotion of soybean uses, planning to use soybeans to manufacture benzene refined oil, food, and other various oils, in order to manipulate soybean prices again. Therefore, the future of soybeans is a problem worthy of attention. (Tohoku News Agency)

Japanese Set Up Hospital in Pangjiang: The Hospital Is a Disguised Espionage Agency

Beijing Correspondence: The Japanese have long coveted Inner Mongolia. Recently, they established a hospital near the De Wang Mansion in Pangjiang. Although it is called a hospital, it is actually a disguised espionage agency. The Japanese in the hospital engage in various activities. The Chahar Provincial Government has repeatedly lodged protests, but the Japanese claim that they will withdraw the hospital after the Chahar Provincial Government establishes a hospital in Pangjiang. The Chahar authorities are planning to establish an Inner Mongolia Hospital in the area. Song Zheyuan, Chairman of Chahar, arrived in Beiping from Zhangjiakou last night. At 10 p.m., he accompanied Qin Dechun and Xiao Zhenying to the Jurentang to meet with He Yingqin to report on the inspection in Pangjiang. (20th)

Various Products in Jiangxi Province Decline Sharply: Exports Decrease by 90 Percent; Trade Deficit Reaches More Than 30 Million Yuan

Nanchang Correspondence: Jiangxi Province has fertile land, a dense population, abundant agricultural products, and many famous handicrafts. Before 1928 and 1929, export trade was increasing day by day. For example, in the 31st year of the Guangxu reign, the total value of exports was 18.9 million yuan. By 1928, it had increased to 61.4 million yuan, an increase of more than three times in twenty years, and it often maintained a trade surplus. In 1919, exports were 53.4 million yuan, with a trade surplus of 23.8 million yuan. In recent years, exports have declined sharply, and imports have increased sharply, forming a contrary picture. For example, cigarette imports have increased forty times in twenty years, and kerosene, steel, and other products have increased more than ten times. By 1931, there was a trade deficit of 35,233,000 yuan, and exports were almost extinct. Money flowed out, forming a state of blood depletion. The decline of various special products is briefly described as follows:

Rice: There is no land in Jiangxi Province that does not produce rice. According to general estimates, the annual rice production is always more than 66 million *dan*. The amount exported through Jiujiang was 2.4 million *dan* in 1924, worth 17 million yuan, but later decreased to 128,000 *dan*, a decrease of 95 percent. In the past two years, we have relied on foreign rice for disaster relief.

Porcelain: The porcelain of Jingdezhen has a history of thousands of years and is famous overseas. During its heyday, there were more than 10,000 porcelain factories, with more than 100,000 porcelain workers. The total value of the products was 20 million taels of silver. All countries in the world were markets for our porcelain. According to the statistics of the Jiujiang Gutang Customs, our country's porcelain exports have decreased from 127,000 *dan* to 50,000 *dan*, a decrease of 61 percent. Recently, it has become even more precarious.

Ramie Cloth: The ramie cloth produced in Wanzai, Yihuang, Pingxiang, Yichun, Chongren, Linchuan, Qianshan, Yushan, Guangchang, Ningdu, and other places is the most common household handicraft. In 1930, 24,000 *dan* were exported, worth more than 6.7 million yuan, but it soon decreased to 3,700 *dan*, a decrease of 82 percent. Recently, it has become unspeakable.

Paper: The province produces bamboo everywhere, which is a natural raw material for papermaking. Qianshan, Guangfeng, Guixi, and fifty of the province's eighty-one counties produce tea. The annual output is about 500,000 *dan*. In 1923, exports reached 329,800 *dan*, worth 20 million yuan, and sales spread throughout Europe and the United States. Recently, it has decreased to 65,400 *dan*, a decrease of 80 percent. Although there are no statistics for last year, it is undeniable that it is getting worse and worse.

Tobacco: Tobacco such as that from Guangfeng and Guangchang is of excellent quality. The annual output is about 330,000 *dan*. Exports have decreased from 215,000 *dan* to 33,000 *dan*, a decrease of 85 percent.

Tungsten Ore: Southern Jiangxi is full of tungsten ore, which is a rare and valuable metal. The output accounts for 60 percent of the world's total. The amount exported from Jiujiang reached more than 100,000 *dan* in 1926, worth more than 2 million yuan. The amount exported from Guangdong must be even greater. Recently, most of the producing areas have fallen into the hands of bandits, and sales have plummeted. Other products such as jute, sesame, soybean oil, and cowhide, as well as various other products, are almost all declining. (March 15)

Fujian Province Bans Opium: Implementing a General Inspection; Special Inspectors from the Headquarters Arrive for Review; The Provincial Government Also Appoints Special Commissioners for Each District

Fuzhou Correspondence: Fujian Province is an absolutely prohibited opium planting province, and also a relatively prohibited opium smoking province. Therefore, although opium paste is contracted by merchants through the Opium Suppression Inspectorate for sales, opium seedlings are still ordered by the provincial government to be eradicated by various counties. The areas that have been most heavily producing opium, such as the counties of Fuan, Fuding, Ningde, and Xiapu in Eastern Fujian, the counties of Anxi, Tong'an, Jinjiang, and Hui'an in Southern Fujian, and the counties of Zhao'an, Yunxiao, Yongding, and Shanghang in Western Fujian, have mostly reported that eradication is complete. Now, in order to urge inspection, increase efficiency, and the current headquarters has specially appointed Gao Hailan as a special inspector for the suppression of opium planting in Fujian, and will jointly implement a general inspection with the provincial government. Gao has already arrived in Fujian for many days and has set up an office on Daoshan Road in the city. The provincial government has appointed Liu Jitang as the special commissioner for the suppression of opium planting in the first administrative district, Zhao Qinglian as the special commissioner for the second district, Wang Yawu as the special commissioner for the third and tenth districts, Huang Yixiong as the special commissioner for the fourth district, Shen Yuchun as the special commissioner for the fifth district, Sun Tongxi as the special commissioner for the sixth district, and Liao Ji as the special commissioner for the seventh, eighth, and ninth districts, all under the command of the special inspection commissioner, and will go to various districts to implement inspections. It can be seen that the districts to which the appointed special commissioners belong include the first district, which is Chang Le; the second district, which is Fu An; the fourth district, which is Xian You; the fifth district, which is Tong An; and the sixth district, which is Zhang Pu; all of which are opium planting areas, and the inspection procedures are very complicated. Therefore, a special commissioner is appointed for each district. The third district is Nan Ping, and the tenth district is Pu Cheng. The climate is cold and it is not suitable for opium planting. The seventh district is Shao Wu, the eighth district is Long Yan, and the ninth district is Chang Ting. All are newly recovered areas, and opium seedlings have long been cleared. The inspection procedures are relatively simple. Therefore, one special commissioner is appointed for every two or three districts. As for the expenses of the opium suppression special commissioner, the entire monthly budget must be more than 4,000 yuan, which is designated by the headquarters to be allocated from the special tax revenue of the Opium Suppression Inspectorate in this province, including the special commissioner's salary of 140 yuan, the staff member's salary of 50 yuan, the clerk's salary of 20 yuan, the public servant's wages of 14 yuan, the special commissioner's food and lodging expenses of 90 yuan, the staff member's food and lodging expenses of 60 yuan, the clerk's food and lodging expenses of 45 yuan, the public servant's food and lodging expenses of 24 yuan, the boat and vehicle expenses of each staff member and public servant of about 100 yuan, and special expenses such as pens, ink, paper, printing, postal and telegraph expenses of 50 yuan per month, totaling 604 yuan per district per month. However, the position of special commissioner is mostly filled by personnel transferred from the provincial government and various listening offices, so they only receive their original salary and do not receive additional pay. Now, as soon as each special commissioner is ready, they can set off. As for the matter of opium suppression, it will be implemented starting from Minhou County in the province. The county government has formulated and issued twelve articles of the measures for issuing opium cessation permits within a limited time, seven articles of the opium cessation measures for opium addicts, and ten articles of the opium addict's self-initiated opium cessation registration certificate form, ordering the various district offices to comply with and handle them, and announcing them to all opium addicts in the county. Those who cannot quit opium immediately due to old age or illness may report the reasons to the various districts and apply for a license in accordance with the prescribed procedures. Those who voluntarily quit opium should also report to the district office and issue a self-initiated opium cessation registration certificate within a limited time. Those who disobey or wait and see and delay in applying for a license will be arrested and sent to the county's opium cessation hospital for compulsory treatment, and will be severely punished according to law. (April 20)

Suzhou: The Relocation of the High Court to Zhenjiang Has Been Called Off

Three months ago, there was talk of relocating the Jiangsu Higher Court to Zhenjiang. The public interest groups of Wu County and the lawyers' associations of Changshu, Haimen, and other places submitted petitions to the Ministry of Judicial Administration, requesting a postponement. According to news from the High Court, the proposal to relocate the High Court to Zhenjiang has now been abandoned. It is planned to set up a Fifth Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court in Zhenjiang, and the old site of the Provincial Government has been designated as the location of the court. The Suzhou High Court has jurisdiction over the appeals of twenty-five counties, including Wu County, Changshu, Wujin, Wuxi, Wujiang, Kunshan, Yixing, Jingjiang, Nantong, Rugao, Taixing, Jiangyin, Shanghai, Songjiang, Fengxian, Nanhui, Baoshan, Chongming, Haimen, Jinshan, Qingpu, Chuansha, Taicang, Jiading, and Qidong. The appeals of the other twenty-four counties, including Jiangpu, are handled by the Fifth Branch. The above plan is expected to be implemented this year.

Land and Water Police Units Defend Against and Suppress Lake Bandits

Recently, large groups of lake bandits have been frequently discovered along Tai Lake, intending to cause trouble. Fortunately, after the joint suppression by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang land and water police units, the lake bandits have fled separately, and the residents near the lake can live in peace. However, although these lake bandits have fled, there is still the possibility of them regrouping. Therefore, Zhou, the district chief of the Second District of the Water Police, and Nie, the captain of the Security Brigade, convened a meeting in Suzhou yesterday with the security captains of various counties such as Wujiang to discuss the issue of joint defense. At that time, it was decided that if bandit groups are discovered, they should cooperate in suppressing them regardless of territorial boundaries, and Wujiang will send a team to patrol various places near the lake to prevent unforeseen events.

Young Girl Dies from Abortion

Yang Ada, a female worker at the Qingfeng Second Yarn Factory in Zhoushanbang, nicknamed "Bai'er Gou," is from Gushan, Jiangyin. She currently lives at No. 3 Xiaocaichang, Zhoushanbang, in this county. At nineteen years old, she is fond of dressing up. Last autumn, she became acquainted with Qian Huangen, the manager of the Jiaotong Rubber Company on Tonghui Road. Their love grew deeper, and they wished to grow old together. However, Qian already had a legal wife, Cao, and was hesitating. Then, Cao suddenly died. Qian immediately decided to formally marry Ada in November of this year. However, Ada was already pregnant. Qian was afraid that she would be heavily pregnant at the wedding, causing ridicule, so he bought an abortion pill and made Ada take it. However, the drug was too strong, and she suffered severe abdominal pain. She died on the 18th of this month, a tragic end.

One Thief Robs Two Families in a Row

In Sifang Lane, near Chenshu Town in the seventh district of the county, the home of farmer Zhu Aba was suddenly broken into by a thief in the middle of the night the other day. The thief pried open the door and dragged Aba out of bed, tied his hands, and took out a pistol, threatening him in every possible way, forcing him to reveal the location of his hidden silver. The thief searched according to the address. Then, Aba took the opportunity to break free, risked his life to escape, and shouted for help. The neighbors rose up and took up arms to catch the thief. By this time, the thief had already heard and escaped to the roof. Fearing being pursued, he hid in the Rangcun Nunnery about a *li* away. Huang, the old woman who guarded the nunnery, saw the thief and shouted to catch him. The thief immediately knelt down and begged her not to make a sound. Huang felt sorry for him and did not drive him away. Who knew that when the thief left, he robbed her second daughter of a handbag, which contained cash, clothes, and other items, worth more than 50 yuan.

Changzhou: Refugee Tragically Run Over and Killed by Train

Jiang Shunjin, a refugee from Yixing, nineteen years old, recently fled the famine with his neighbors. At about 4 p.m. on the 20th, a group of eight people carried their belongings, planning to go to Wuxi from Changzhou, walking along the railway. Afterwards, the county court reported the incident, and prosecutor Guan Junjie went to examine the body on the 21st. He instructed the townspeople to prepare a coffin for burial.

Hangzhou Major Fire in Xiaban'er Lane Yesterday Morning

Changfa Southern Goods Store, No. 91, Xiaban'er Lane, Hangzhou, caught fire at 1:10 AM this morning (the 22nd) due to a knocked-over kerosene lamp. Flames erupted instantly, and the fire spread extremely rapidly. After the fire brigade, various fire fighting associations, foreign volunteer firemen, and others made every effort to extinguish it, the fire was finally put out at 2:30 AM. Suicide by Poison Due to Family Issues

Wang Baohe, from Fuyang, has been working in politics and has a wife and a concubine at home. Recently, due to frequent family disputes, Wang suffered considerable emotional distress. He came to Hangzhou alone some time ago, using the alias Zhonghe, staying at the Dongxing Hotel near the city railway station. He secretly purchased sleeping pills and ingested them in an attempt to commit suicide. However, he had written a farewell letter to his wife and concubine beforehand. After receiving the news, they rushed to Hangzhou and found Wang barely alive. He was immediately sent to the hospital for treatment. After the doctor administered acupuncture and gastric lavage, his life was no longer in danger and he is still receiving treatment in the hospital.

Zhu Xiangmao's House Robbed

In Duanwei, southeast of Qidong Jiujiang Town, farmer Zhu Xiangmao, whose family is of modest means, was suddenly visited by seven or eight bandits in the middle of the night. They spoke in mixed dialects, each holding a box gun, and broke into the house. Zhu was awakened from his sleep and escaped through the back door. The bandits then grabbed Zhu's wife, beat her severely with wooden sticks, and demanded that she hand over the hidden money, but failed. They then rummaged through boxes and cabinets, searching at will. At this time, Zhu had gathered villagers, sounded gongs, and lit fires, coming to surround and arrest the bandits. Local News

Amidst a Grand Welcome American Economic Mission Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning To Pay a Visit to Mayor Wu This Morning and Visit the Art Exhibition in the Afternoon To Enter Beijing by Special Train Tonight and Return to Shanghai by Plane Tomorrow Afternoon

The American Far East Economic Mission, a group of eleven people, along with their families, totaling sixteen people, led by the mission leader Forbes, arrived in Shanghai at 8:30 AM yesterday morning aboard the Harrison President from Kobe. Representatives from the reception committee boarded the special "Lihua" boat at 7:00 AM to welcome them. The mission will stay in China for two months, representing American business and economic circles, to investigate the trade relations between the two countries. All investigation matters will be carried out in cooperation with the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the China Council for the Promotion of International Trade, the Shanghai Branch of the International Chamber of Commerce, the Sino-American Trade Association, and other institutions. They are scheduled to pay a visit to Mayor Wu at 10:30 AM this morning, visit the pre-exhibition of the art exhibition in the afternoon, and enter Beijing by special train at 11:00 PM tonight. The Central News Agency reporter has compiled the details as follows:

Welcoming Personnel

The Harrison President entered the port at 4:00 AM yesterday morning and docked at the Dalae Wharf in Bailianjing, Pudong. Representatives from the reception committee and various groups boarded the special boat "Lihua" of the Jianghai Customs at 7:00 AM to welcome them. Mayor Wu's representatives, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government Yu Hongjun, and secretaries Zhang Tingrong and Geng Jiaji, also visited the mission beforehand to meet and talk because they were going to welcome the Russian ambassador. Those who arrived included Guo Bingwen, Chen Zeqing, Zhang Xianglin, Pan Guangjiong, Zhu Shaoping of the Global Student Association, Liu Hongen of the International Problems Research Association, Fan Zhenchu of the Road Association, Cao Yunxiang of the Returned Students Association, Lu Ganchen of the YMCA, Chen Liting of the Pacific Society, Xu Shanxiang of the Chinese Institute of Engineers, Wang Xiaolai of the Aviation Association, Xu Xinliu of the Bankers Association, Nie Lusheng of the China General Federation of Industries, Xi Jimin of the Money Trade Association, He Dekui of the China Economic Society, Guo Dehua and Hou Aichang of the National Economic Committee, American Vice Consul Remy, Frank L. Huppikin and Bysart of the American Chamber of Commerce, and Kondick and McNo of the mission in Shanghai. Zhang Xianglin directed the traffic, and the manager of the International Hotel also went to take care of everything.

Arrival Situation

The welcoming personnel all wore badges welcoming the American Economic Mission, with the flags of the two countries engraved on them, and a blue-bottomed gold-lettered silk banner attached below. After boarding the large ship, they were led by Guo Bingwen and Chen Zeqing, and mission member Remer was invited to meet with mission leader Forbes and present a welcome letter. Everyone went up to the reception room, exchanged greetings and introductions, and distributed commemorative badges to the mission. They then took a group photo of the mission and the reception committee on the deck. After the mission and the reception committee took separate photos, everyone boarded the "Lihua" boat and arrived at the New Customs Wharf at 8:40 AM. They boarded more than ten new-style cars of uniform style and went directly to the reserved rooms in the International Hotel to rest. As the mission had just arrived, they visited friends after lunch and went shopping in the city. In the evening, all mission members gathered to discuss the itinerary and plans for the investigation.

Mission Members Arriving in Shanghai

Mission Leader Forbes (former Governor-General of the Philippines, American Ambassador to Japan), Deputy Leader Carroll (former General Manager of the Persian National Railway and Chief Engineer of the Hubei-Guangdong Railway in China), Secretary Storreld (journalist), Accountant Shively, Mission Members Delingham, Rogers, Remer, Herdon, Wickham, Jones, Bexbey (joined from Japan), and family members of the mission members, totaling sixteen people. Mission members Kondick and McNo are also participating in Shanghai.

Welcome Letter

The welcome letter from the reception committee to the mission is as follows: Dear Mr. Forbes, We, the reception committee, extend our sincere welcome to you and the members of the American Economic Mission on your visit to China. We wish you a pleasant trip and we are willing to do our best to help you achieve satisfactory results in your investigation in China. Attached is a list of the welcoming personnel who boarded the ship, please check. Zhang Jia'ao.

Mission Leader's Speech

Mission Leader Forbes issued a written statement upon arriving in Shanghai, saying, "I believe that this is the most thorough investigation by American business circles to this great country. The special development of air transport in China is of great help to this investigation. I deeply believe that this is the first time that a delegation of American business representatives has traveled to the new China by plane to conduct a detailed and extensive investigation. The railway and air travel programs have been arranged, which will be of great benefit to the work of the mission. The purpose of the mission's visit to China is to study the past, present, and future business relations between China and the United States. There are no government representatives or financial assistance in the American Economic Mission. The mission's motives and all expenses are borne by American industrial, commercial, and banking circles and states that have relations with the Far East. All members of the mission are the most relevant people in American banking, food, tobacco, textile, aviation, and shipping industries. Although the mission does not have a specific investigation task, we will do our best to promote the increase in trade between the two countries. We are fact-finders and have no executive power. The whole mission should have a common understanding and desire for the principles of developing trade between the two countries, which is the most important task in our minds. On behalf of the mission, I would like to express my deep gratitude to Mr. Zhang Fu'ao, Chairman of the reception committee, and the representatives of the reception committee, for providing various conveniences for us. After visiting Beijing and meeting with the government authorities of your country, we will return to Shanghai and exchange views with the leaders of the Shanghai business community. After that, the whole mission will tour the north, south, and central parts of China and meet with local Chinese business leaders. Another group will visit the Philippines. After the entire trip is completed, the whole mission will gather in Shanghai and collect the materials obtained to hold a final consultation with the leaders of the Shanghai business community.

Today's Itinerary

All members of the mission are scheduled to gather at 9:45 AM this morning and visit Mayor Wu at the Municipal Government in the city center at 10:30 AM, accompanied by Guo Bingwen. According to the Municipal Government's announcement, Mayor Wu was touring Hangzhou and is scheduled to rush back last night to prepare for the meeting. The Sino-American Trade Association will host a banquet at the American Club at noon, and the family members will be hosted by the American Women's Association. At 2:30 PM in the afternoon, they will depart from the International Hotel and go to the Bund on Renji Road to visit the Chinese pre-exhibition of the London Art Exhibition. At 11:00 PM tonight, they will enter Beijing by special train, accompanied by Hou Aichang of the National Economic Committee. Li Yushu, a section chief from the two railway bureaus, will also be sent to take care of them. The members of the mission will return to Shanghai by Douglas aircraft of the China National Aviation Corporation at 4:00 PM on the 25th.

The members of the mission are scheduled to arrive in Beijing at 7:00 AM on the 24th and go to the Huilong Hotel to rest. At 9:00 AM, they will visit the mausoleum and lay wreaths. Tongtai Zhuang Suspended Business Yesterday

Wu and Chen, the lawyers representing the liquidation of Xinsheng News Agency, said that the Shanghai industrial and commercial situation will soon reach the bottom of the fourth quarter. Following the suspension of business liquidation of Yongxing Qianzhuang, a member of the Money Trade Association, a few days ago, Tongtai Shunji Qianzhuang also suspended business liquidation yesterday morning due to insufficient capital turnover. The details are as follows:

History of the Qianzhuang

Tongtai Huihua Qianzhuang was established in January of the tenth year of the Republic of China with a total capital of 340,000 yuan. The shareholders were originally Tan Bushao (six shares), Le Zhenbao (two shares), Tan Zilin (one share), and Huang Zhenrong (one share), a total of ten shares. The manager was Fu Yuzhai and the associate manager was Chuan Yujing. The address was No. 240 Ningbo Road, North City. During the year-end closing in the twenty-third year of the Republic of China, it was successfully reorganized. Shareholders Le Zhenbao and Huang Zhenrong split their shares, Tan Bushao increased his shares by two to eight shares, and Tan Zilin increased his shares by one to two shares. It was also renamed Tongtai Shunji. The manager and associate manager remained the same.

Difficulty the Night Before

The Qianzhuang's business volume is quite large, always over one or two million yuan. Now, due to the impact of the poor market situation, the loans issued, such as long-term credit, overdrafts, and mortgages, cannot be recovered. The Qianzhuang lacks circulating funds. At 8:00 PM the night before, the difference between the amount received and the amount disbursed was very large, resulting in insufficient capital turnover and a very dangerous situation. Fortunately, manager Fu Yuzhai and Fu Yujing rushed around and the shareholders advanced money to maintain the business and overcome the difficulty. Therefore, the Qianye Tongye Gonghui (Money Trade Association) note from the Qianzhuang last night was also cleared in full.

Decision to Suspend Business

Bank of Communications Held a Board Meeting Yesterday Two Additional Standing Directors Elected Chairman and General Manager Remain the Same

The Central News Agency reports that after the Bank of Communications increased government shares by 10 million yuan, which was approved by the shareholders' meeting, the Ministry of Finance appointed Wang Rutang and seven others to serve as government-share directors and supervisors. All directors and supervisors of the bank held separate meetings yesterday afternoon and elected Song Ziliang and Yang Xiaofu as standing directors. There were no changes to the chairman and general manager. The details are recorded below:

Two Additional Standing Directors Elected

The first board meeting of the Bank of Communications after the increase in share capital was held at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon in the conference room on the fourth floor of the bank. The attending government-share directors were Zhang Shouyong, Li Chengyi, Qin Zuce, Wang Rutang, Zhu Ziliang, Yang Dunfu, Xu Xinliu, Yang Xiaotian, Shen Shuyu, and the commercial-share directors were Hu Bijang, Tang Shoumin, Qian Yongming, Hu Zutong, Zhou Zuomin, Li Ming, Wang Chengzhu, Chen Huide, Ye Fuji, Yang Desen, etc. Qian Yongming was temporarily elected as chairman. After the ceremony, the chairman reported that after the increase in government shares, according to the 14th article of the revised regulations, there should be seven standing directors, and two more should be elected. After mutual election, Song Ziliang and Yang Dunfu were elected as standing directors. The terms of the original standing directors have not expired, so there were no changes.

Chairman and General Manager Remain in Office

According to the regulations, the chairman of the bank must be appointed by the Ministry of Finance from among the standing directors, and the general manager must be selected by the chairman in consultation with the standing directors from among the directors and appointed with the approval of the board of directors. Since the current chairman Hu Bijang and general manager Tang Shoumin took office, the business has made rapid progress. The total assets of the bank this year have increased by as much as 70 million yuan compared to the previous year. Both government and business parties have expressed their trust in them, so the two men were re-elected. After discussion by the board of directors, it was decided that Song Ziliang and Qian Xinzhi would visit Finance Minister Kong to report and bring the commission letter for addition.

Supervisory Meeting Held at the Same Time

The supervisory meeting was held at the same time in the bank. The attending government-share supervisors were Xu Xiuzhi, Zhang Xiaolin, and Zhao Dihua, and the commercial-share supervisors were Ye Chongxun, Zou Minchu, and Jia Shiyi, etc. Zhao Dihua chaired the meeting. After the ceremony, the chairman reported that according to Article 24 of the bank's articles of association, one resident supervisor should be elected. As a result, Xu Xiuzhi was still elected to serve.

No Changes to Internal Organization

According to reporters, after the increase in shareholders in the bank, in addition to the Ministry of Finance adding eight directors and supervisors, there were no changes to the internal organization. However, in the past, all bank affairs were handled by the general manager, but now it is stipulated that standing directors must also go to the bank regularly to perform their duties, so their business will develop more and more. The result of the meeting was that the loans issued were difficult to recover for a while, and the dangerous atmosphere outside had been leaked. If all depositors rush to withdraw money, it will be impossible to cope with. It was decided to suspend business starting yesterday morning, so the Qianzhuang suspended business yesterday morning.

Announce Liquidation

After the Qianzhuang decided to suspend business, it entrusted Wu Linkun and Chen Zhongyin, lawyers from the Tongren Law Office, to announce the suspension of business liquidation. The lawyer's announcement stated, "Recently, Fu Yuzhai, manager of Tongtai Shunji Zhuang, and Fu Yujing, deputy manager, stated that our Zhuang has been affected by the poor market situation, resulting in insufficient capital turnover, and we have to suspend business liquidation of accounts. For this reason, we entrust your lawyers to announce to the public that all debtors are required to go to our Zhuang liquidation office within 14 days to pay off debts. Overdue debts will not be handled and will be pursued according to law. As for all creditors, it is also hoped that within 14 days, they will bring their debt certificates to register at our Zhuang liquidation office." Therefore, this special announcement is made to the right, please take note. April 22.
