Recent News from the Individual Track and Field Promotion Association

A Glimpse of Association Affairs The China Individual Track and Field Competition Promotion Association has attracted much attention from the community since its establishment in November of last year. Now, Jinan, Nanchang, and other places have successively organized individual sports events. Now, in order to actively carry out its work, the association has decided to host the Shanghai Municipal Track and Field Meet on May 26, and at the same time invite the sports and news circles in Shanghai to hold a get-together. It is also scheduled to host the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Beijing, and Shanghai four-province/city long-distance running championship in June. Generalissimo Jiang specially donated 200 yuan to the association for this municipal track and field meet.

Source of Funds As for the economic source of the association, it has been established for half a year and has received the strong support of various circles. Generalissimo Jiang donated 200 yuan, Dean Wang donated 20 yuan, Minister Zhu donated 100 yuan, Minister of Cadres 100 yuan, Zhang Hanqing 40 yuan, Mayor Wu 40 yuan, Cheng Yize 19 yuan, Xue Xuehai 18 yuan, Xu Zhiyi 10 yuan, Ruan Weicun 100 yuan, and membership fee income was 105.3 yuan. In total, from November 1 of last year to the 20th of this month, the total revenue item was 702.3 yuan. The expenditure items are divided into five categories, totaling 498.1 yuan.

Municipal Field Manager Since its establishment, the association has hosted more than 20 sports events, large and small, with nearly 2,000 participants, making it a powerful organization for promoting mass sports. This time, the association will host the Municipal Track and Field Meet in Shen Garden and has received a large number of prizes from President Chen of the Central Bank, Supervisor Tang of the Jianghai Customs, Tianchu, Land Bureau, Commercial Press, and China.

Statement of Errors When the association released the news a few days ago, two errors occurred. (1) The association omitted the 10,000-meter event in the competition program. Also, the association's invitation to Shao Rugan to serve as the general manager is the general manager of the Municipal Track and Field Meet, not the general manager of the Individual Track and Field Meet. As for the public letters that the association distributed to the schools a few days ago to solicit participation, this kind of error occurred.

Mr. Shao Rugan's Statement

This newspaper received a letter from Shao yesterday saying that the China Individual Track and Field Competition Promotion Association plans to hold the Shanghai Municipal Track and Field Sports Meet in Shen Garden on May 26. The organizer invited me to serve as the general manager. Rugan had verbally agreed to assist. It is now found that in the association's recent external documents, in addition to the association's stamp, there is also a wooden stamp of the words "General Manager Shao Mou" co-signed. Without my prior consent, I am afraid there will be misunderstandings. I hereby declare. Shao Rugan, April 22.

My Philosophy on Officiating Basketball (I)

— Written by American J. Dahl, Translated by Qian Yiqin

This article, written by the famous American basketball referee J. Dahl, was published in the American sports monthly in February of this year. Its ideas are fresh, and its theories are detailed and precise. It is translated here as a reference for us. - The Translator

First and foremost, the author wants to make it clear to the reader that he has no intention of teaching others how to act as a basketball referee. He firmly believes that this is not an easy task. A refereeing method that works for one person may be the opposite for another, rendering them useless. Although there are indeed fixed rules to follow in terms of mechanical procedures, each referee should strive to develop their own personality and skills. All of this can only be achieved through diligent work and practice. No referee or school of referees should try to instill their particular personality and skills into others.

It must be reiterated that this article is not intended to be followed literally by the reader. It should be understood that the material in this article is merely an expression of the author's sincere thoughts, as he has a great interest in basketball games and officiating.

The author would be most fortunate if the reader agrees with some or all of these views. If not, disagreement is only natural and nothing to be surprised about, as differing opinions are an element that drives the world forward.

To become a successful and outstanding referee, it must come from hard work and practice, as mentioned earlier. Here is a golden rule for those who aspire to be successful and well-known referees: "Call the game as you see it, without bias, without fear, and in accordance with the rules."

Criticism is Inevitable. It is inevitable for referees to be criticized, and this is the first thing that anyone acting as a referee must know. It is extremely rare for a referee to receive praise from all sides after a game. If the enforcement is strict, it is bound to draw criticism from some. If it is too lenient, it will surely be met with backlash from others. Even if the enforcement is selfless and fearless, harsh criticism is unavoidable. Even if judgments are made according to the psychology of the audience, players, or coaches, it is impossible to avoid criticism. Therefore, no matter how one officiates, there will always be critics.

If a referee is negligent during a rough game, protests from the players will pour in, not to mention the criticism from coaches and spectators. If someone thinks there are too many free throws, they will definitely be criticized. Even people associated with a team may want the referee to be lenient if their team has large players, but then ask for strict enforcement if their players are smaller the following season, which is extremely difficult.

From this perspective, the only safe method for a referee is to "call it as you see it, according to the rules." Only in this way can one be sure of being correct despite the criticism, and have a clear conscience. Conversely, if a referee is lenient, they will know they have been negligent when criticism arrives and will have no ground to stand on. However, no matter how one officiates, criticism is unavoidable. Those who are referees should get used to it.

The rules are set by the rules committee to enhance skills (such as passing and shooting) and to avoid the rough play of basketball games of the past. Although some people believe that basketball games are getting worse, this is only the view of a very small minority. As far as the author knows, millions of players (old or young), coaches, and spectators do not think so. Upon thorough investigation, coaches or players (and even spectators) prefer games that are officiated according to the spirit of the rules to those that are officiated leniently, as they are much more interesting.

The author has personally experienced the following: In one game, the two teams were fierce rivals, and conflict was unavoidable. However, the referees were quite surprised during the game because, although the competition was intense, it was quite clean. What was even more surprising was that after the game, the captain of one of the teams (which was known for being rough) said to the referee, "The game was good tonight, thanks to your efforts." The referee replied, "I don't know about that, maybe it's because your game was so clean that we didn't have much to do." The captain then made a surprising reply: "Let me tell you, the coach told us to try our best to play ball tonight, so we forgot to hit people."

There is more to say. Sometimes, after a clean game, a few spectators may come to the referees to express their appreciation for the good officiating. If the game is rough, someone will definitely come forward after the game to say harsh words, claiming that the referee was a terrible performer. In fact, refereeing is easy in clean games because both sides have good skills. Knowing this, it is clear that a referee in a rough game will not receive good reviews even if they do their best.

Different Perspectives. From another perspective, the referee announces the game from their personal point of view, while the audience and coaches each have their own different perspectives and angles, so what they see will inevitably be different. What appears to be an obvious foul from one angle may not be so from another. Therefore, what the referee sees in a game is one thing, and what the audience sees from the sidelines is another. The reason for this is very clear. If the referee were seated on the sidelines, they would see everything the audience sees, but that is impossible. This reason is particularly true in situations where a dribbling player comes into contact with a defending player.

Of course, many fouls are obvious from all angles, and the audience's judgment is just as good as the referee's. If the referee easily overlooks these obvious fouls at this time, they are only asking for trouble. One more point must be mentioned. It has been heard that referees say, "My officiating depends on the game situation and the coaches' requests. If they like strict, I'm strict; if they like lenient, I'm lenient." The author once heard a referee ask a coach, "How would you like me to officiate tonight, strict or lenient?" This is not the author's intention to nitpick or enjoy commenting on other people's refereeing methods, as it is none of my business. The reason for giving this as an example is that I am deeply afraid that this kind of approach is harmful. The provisions for fouls in the rules are actually to promote the improvement of skills. This definition and the interpretations contained after the rules are very clear. If a referee can make another interpretation, then the responsibility they bear is too heavy. If they can implement the rules as stipulated by the rules committee, they will definitely get good results.

Tidbits

— (Yan Xin-quan)

If there were two envelopes, one made of domestic paper requiring one copper coin, and one made of foreign paper requiring only five cash, then I dare say, "Everyone would know to choose the cheaper one, without even considering foreign or domestic goods!" I remember Mr. Chen Bulei once said, "To promote domestic goods, one must have some foolishness and some courage to reap the benefits." This is truly well said!

"The number of literate people is greatly related to the strength of a country." This is something no one can deny. Therefore, in recent years, literacy campaigns have been launched everywhere, with widespread publicity to encourage the public to become literate. Although the tools they use for publicity include performances, speeches, etc., posting slogans is also considered an important task. Phrases like "Illiterate people are blind" are almost everywhere. However, I think "to use words to persuade illiterate people is somewhat contradictory, isn't it?"

Swallow

— Zhu Shao-fei

One morning, after a spring slumber, when I woke up, the sun was already high in the sky. A murmur of singing reached my ears. The swallows had arrived! Feeling joyful, I excitedly strolled to the hall to welcome them.

Watching their scissor-like wings, they flew in pairs, sometimes swirling inside the hall, sometimes flying outside the patio wall.

Because I was so fond of swallows, out of loving care, I moved a ladder and nailed two nails onto the beams for them to perch on and build their nest, and hung a bamboo basket underneath to catch the droppings. The nails were for them to lean on while building their nest, and the basket was to catch the droppings that would fall.

Every day, I would remember to stroll over there and stare at them once or twice. They were diligently carrying mud mixed with bits of rice straw to build their nest. I noticed how difficult it was for them to carry the mud, probably because the mud was sticky, but this mud could only be found on the distant shores of Taihu Lake.

Watching them carry the mud, the damp mud nest gradually dried, and only then did their nest-building project come to an end.

There were probably eggs in the nest. Hearing my footsteps, a swallow sitting in the nest poked its head out, glanced at me, and then quietly retreated back inside.

Thinking back to my childhood, when I knew the swallows were hiding inside, it meant they were incubating eggs. I would always steal the eggs to play with. When my mom saw me, she would always scare me by saying, "Taking swallow eggs will cause you to get swallow sores." But I was not afraid. Once the egg was in my hand, I would break it and be done with it. And I didn't care about the anxious state of the old swallow after losing its egg, endlessly calling out in the hall. Now, I think it was too cruel, and I can't bring myself to do it anymore. Let them hatch their lovely baby swallows.

Small Habits

— Zhou Xian

I have a habit recently of paying attention to my friends' small habits.

My supervisor, Mr. Sun, is very young. His chin is shaved clean every day, but he can't say three sentences without touching his chin with his hand.

My colleague, Lao Li, has a habit of scratching his scalp. While talking to people, he often uses the ring finger of his right hand to scratch his scalp, and always exactly twice.

There is also a colleague, Lao Chen, who always lifts the hem of his long gown with his left hand when standing. This and his younger brother, Xiao Chen, who wears a suit, constantly unbuttons and buttons his coat buttons when talking to people, can be said to be a perfect match, with different tunes but the same effect.

A-Liang, also a colleague, often twitches the outer corner of his right eye and the right corner of his mouth up and down when talking to people, as if making eyes at them. But when no one is talking to him, his eye corners and mouth corners remain still and motionless.

Secretary Ms. Hu often wraps a small handkerchief around the ring finger of her right hand. When she sits alone thinking, she wraps the handkerchief around her finger so much. When talking to people, she wraps the handkerchief around her finger so much. Sometimes I sit with her on a tram going back, and I see her wrapping the handkerchief around her finger there too.

Ms. Liu, also a colleague, doesn't have lung disease, but always makes a light cough or two when speaking. When she is not speaking, the coughing also stops.

These small habits don't seem to be worth paying attention to, but if you pay attention once or twice, you will find it very funny the next time you see these expressions.

The Destination of the New Woman

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 12: Ashamed of Having No Clothes, She Curtains Herself Off from Guests; Diligently Saves Lamp Oil, She Copies Books at Dawn

Yueying was quite thirsty, so she reached her arm out from the tent door to take the teacup inside. After drinking, she again sent the cup out with her arm. The two arms, going in and out of the tent door, prevented Beihai from focusing on his books, and he kept gazing at the tent. He said, "It's not a good solution for you to sleep on Mr. Cheng's bed all the time. You should urge your family to bring you clothes to change as soon as possible." Yueying said, "Where would I have clothes to change? My aunt took the wet clothes to bake dry. Once they are dry, she will naturally bring them." Beihai said, "The last time I saw you wearing clothes, the style was very new. Do you only have that one set?" Yueying said, "Those clothes were borrowed from the servants here." Beihai said, "If they were borrowed from the servants here, then you originally had a set of clothes?" Yueying said, "Those clothes were also given to our three generations by a high-ranking official we met in Pingliang while coming from the West. The clothes I was originally wearing were too torn to wear." She mentioned coming from the West, which touched Beihai's concerns, because there were many questions he was wondering about, and today was a good time to ask. He said, "I've been thinking about something. Miss Zhu, you lived well in Gansu, so why did you come here?" Yueying said, "It's just that we couldn't make a living. A family of three generations, all women, what kind of outcome is that? We heard that our uncle was performing opera in Xi'an, so we came here, but we didn't expect that our uncle had been dead for a long time." Beihai said, "An opera singer's monthly earnings are also very limited. Even if he were still alive, I don't think he could support a family of three like you." (188)

The Scent of Incense Lingers

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

All other distractions ceased to exist because of their dedication to their duties! So what would be the fate of these women when they grew old? It was, of course, different from that of ordinary old people! By the time they gradually grew old! Probably no more than forty or fifty years old, because the art of embroidery was extremely exhausting and most likely to cause aging! When their eyesight was no longer sufficient to do such fine embroidery work, naturally, new people would come in to replace them, allowing them to stay in the palace and retire, from then on they would no longer be active, simply eating and wearing clothes, lazing around until they passed away peacefully. I think they all had a traditional concept that when they were young and strong and could work as hard as possible, they would devote all their efforts to this beautiful craft; and when they grew old, they would rely on these achievements to live a comfortable life eating free meals in the palace.

Is this concept right? Is it reasonable? Is it beneficial to them? Of course, I cannot answer for them; I cannot even explain why they held this traditional concept. I think unless I had the same skillful hands as them, and constantly embroidered flowers on those satin tributes, and experienced it firsthand, perhaps I would be able to understand the real reason; now, it is absolutely impossible to figure it out by merely imagining!

Didn't I say above that there were four or five shoe patterns outlined on each piece of satin tribute; after they put this piece of satin tribute on the embroidery frame, they would embroider them one by one from top to bottom. (298)

The Life of a Rich Man

— Zhu Ying

I have a friend who is a private tutor in a rich man's home. From my friend, I learned about some interesting snippets of this rich man's life.

This rich man is only in his forties and is the owner of a Heng-character numbered Qian Zhuang (old style bank), two large pawnshops, and a department store with a double-wide storefront. In addition, he naturally has shares in many large businesses. It is said that his movable and immovable property amounts to more than three million, so his concerns are not about the prosperity or decline of his business, but about the arrival of kidnappers.

He was kidnapped once four years ago. Since then, he has specially hired two Russian and four local bodyguards. They are divided into two shifts, patrolling the residence day and night. He usually doesn't go out, lying on his opium bed all day and night. Even when he has to go out, he is protected by at least three bodyguards.

Therefore, his two sons and one daughter do not attend school, for fear of accidents on the way. But to be a tutor in his home, in addition to providing a guarantor when hired, you must also be searched by the bodyguards every day before entering his home. To be a driver, servant, or even a maid in his house, you must have two reliable guarantors.

The windows in his house are never opened throughout the year. The gardens around the residence are also densely covered with barbed wire. Anyone who wants to see him must be interrogated in detail by the accountant in his house, just like a trial. Even my friend, who has been teaching in his house for more than two years, has not seen the owner more than ten times.

Alas, I don't think this kind of life is very enjoyable.

In addition to canceling the payment for the article, we hereby declare this. Also, the article on evaluation written by Hu Ping on April 6 was found to be plagiarized from another newspaper and should be treated in the same way as the above item, and this is also declared.

World News

Miscellaneous News from the Yokohama Exposition (Part 2)

— Ji Yun

The Manchurian and Korean products are displayed as specimens. The annual output of cotton, soybeans, ginseng, and coal and iron ore is in the millions. Due to inconvenient transportation, there are very few products on display. The Siamese Pavilion has snake skins, cow horns, and various grains of rice. The grain is slender and different from our country's, and is often imported to Japan in large quantities. The silver carvings have an ancient Egyptian style that is unmatched by Japan.

Hokkaido produces bears and wood. Farmers in the Yagumo area carve bear statues out of brown wood blocks, with each one priced as high as fifteen yuan. Whether it is a bookend, book clip, or stationery, they are all attached with bear images, and the carving of bears has become their specialized local art. Nara clay figurines are very famous, all made by hand without using machines. The Japanese female figurines they make are exceptionally exquisite, and the colors applied are bright and delicate, surpassing Huishan in Wuxi. There is a statue of Bai Letian, with a solemn and dignified appearance, carved with great precision, but priced at fifteen yuan. China does not have such expensive clay figurines.

Japanese woodwork is more developed than our country's. A single piece of wood can be made into various utensils. The walls of the Hokkaido Wood Specimen Hall are made of thin slices woven into diagonal grids, which is very interesting. Japanese architecture makes flat-roofed houses very quickly. After the wooden frame is erected, reed curtains are used as walls, and some mud ash is applied. Then, a few pieces of paper are pasted, and a mat is laid, and a very beautiful house is built in less than two days. The buildings at the exposition are all of this type, so while some are still being built, some are already damaged. Utilizing waste materials, reducing costs, and having modern styles that cater to people's psychology are the only reasons why Japanese handicrafts sell well. For example, cufflinks for suits are made of crystal, amber, tortoiseshell, gemstones, and pearls. They are all set in alloy, so each piece is only two or three yuan. There are also man-made ones that are only two or three jiao apiece, which can be passed off as genuine. The colors and patterns of glassware are also exceptionally exquisite. Because they have competitions for everything, they all think to the extreme in the hope of defeating others.

Women do not have a high status in Japanese society. But because they are gentle and meticulous, large companies, food stores, and transportation agencies all hire women as clerks, waitresses, and in sales. Female employees make up an even larger number at the exhibition, so now in Japan's workforce, there is already a phenomenon of women replacing men. In addition, Japanese housework is all done by women. Besides working at home, they also have to go out and buy everything. There are also more female visitors at the exhibition than men. We have jokingly called modern Japan a world of women.

Commercial News

Finance: The End of April is Approaching; Tongtai Zhuang Follows Yongxing into Liquidation

Yesterday's foreign market situation, superficially, remained the same, but looking at its inner workings, with the end of April approaching, and the talk of accommodating transfers on the income side, people cannot be forced to pay. On the payout side, due to credit relations, one has to reluctantly pay. The difference between inflows and outflows is huge. Yongxing had already collapsed earlier, and yesterday, Tongtai Shun Ji followed suit. Fortunately, the bills of exchange of this Zhuang have no close relationship with other parties, so it will not affect the market. Yesterday, the discount rate in the market was one jiao in both the morning and afternoon markets. The overnight interest rate still opened at three fen, which was no different from the past few days. In the morning market, bill of exchange transactions amounted to over 3.5 million, and new transactions amounted to over 300,000. In the afternoon market, transactions amounted to over 300,000. Free Talk

Modern Masters' Speeches

— Chen Zizhan

"Speech" is one of the four subjects of Confucius' school. It is listed alongside "Virtue," "Politics," and "Literature," showing that Confucius regarded "Speech" as a very important subject. In fact, during the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods, the art of speech had already reached a very high level. As long as you have read books like "Zuo Zhuan," "Guo Yu," and "Strategies of the Warring States," you will know that in this era, not only the envoys of various countries, the so-called "officials of foreign affairs," and the persuaders, the so-called "strategists," had to pay attention to "speech," but also everyone else knew how to speak. In addition, "The Analects of Confucius," which records the words and deeds of Confucius and Mencius, "Mozi," which records the words and deeds of Mo Di, and the later "Book of Rites: Tan Gong," which record many dialogues, debates, and talks, although they are like recorded sayings for preaching and teaching, are very elegant and are no less than excellent ancient literature. Of course, we also know that the ancients believed that "words that are not refined will not travel far." Even though the records of "speech" at that time were inevitably embellished, we cannot deny that Confucius' school separated "speech" and "literature," and that "speech" was a kind of learning in itself at that time.

The recorded sayings of eminent monks and great Confucian scholars since the Tang and Song dynasties are all words for preaching and teaching, focusing not on "speech" or "literature." However, they seemed to have already realized that "literature to clarify the Dao" could not clarify it, and "literature to carry the Dao" could not carry it, so they had to switch to spoken language. They recorded their lectures, their dialogues and debates with teachers and friends, all in spoken language, which was naturally more authentic than using ancient prose. But in terms of literary value, apart from being an attempt at spoken language writing, it really has little literary flavor in itself. Therefore, catalogue scholars have always listed recorded sayings in the "philosophy" category, as philosophical books, and would not put them in the "collected works" category, as literary books. We know that in ancient Greece and Rome, speeches such as those of Demosthenes and Cicero had long become a category of literature. However, in China, it must be said that it is only recently that there has been a category of speeches in the department of literature in library catalogs.

Now, as I compile this selection of famous speeches, except for Mr. Liang Rengong, who has passed away, the rest are all alive and well. There are twelve recorded speeches in total, by eleven authors from Zhang Taiyan and Liang Rengong to John Dewey. Only Mr. Dewey is a foreigner, with two speeches recorded. The earliest speech is that of Mr. Zhang Taiyan, recorded exactly thirty years ago. Mr. Zhang was imprisoned in 1903 (the 29th year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing dynasty) for advocating "anti-Manchu" and "revolution" in the Shanghai Subao case. After three years in prison, he went to Japan on June 29, 1905, immediately after his release from prison. This is his speech at the welcome meeting for comrades in Japan, published in the sixth issue of the Minbao, the organ magazine of the Min Party at that time. Mr. Zhang's autobiography of his life is an extremely valuable material. The most recent speech is Mr. Jiang Menglin's "How Should We Study?" This is Mr. Jiang's speech on the Tianjin Youth Association Broadcasting Station, published in the Tianjin Dagongbao in February of this year, and has not yet been compiled by other books. Among these eleven figures, some are scholars of Sinology or writers, some are philosophers or educators, some are revolutionaries, and some are scientists. Their speeches talk about how to be a person, how to be a revolutionary, how to be a writer, and how to be a scientist. Some talk about how to study hard and how to cultivate oneself academically; some talk about how to hone one's morality and how to cultivate oneself personally. Their expertise may be specialized, and their thoughts and opinions may not be consistent, but they are united in their positive spirit and their efforts to progress. I have compiled their speeches together as a kind of reading material for young friends, which may be of some help in their cultivation of learning and conduct.

Of course, in such a small book, it is impossible to collect all the speeches of famous people in the country, and besides, some who are called famous people may not have any wonderful speeches to record. As for foreign famous scholars who have come to China to lecture, there are also Russell and Driesch, but here I have only selected Dewey's speeches, because his thoughts and theories are not as difficult to understand as Russell's mathematical logic or Driesch's organic philosophy. But I have to state that in the past ten years, due to the progress of the Chinese intellectual world, Dewey's pragmatism has gradually lost its authority in China during the "May Fourth" era.

Here, two lectures by Dewey are selected, one titled "Morality and Human Nature" and the other titled "The Place of Emotions in Morality." He advocates a positive and progressive morality, opposes the passive restraint of instincts, and advocates cultivating correct ideas and arousing and promoting vigorous emotions. Currently in China, most of our young people are either obsequiously flattering the world or are dispirited and muddleheaded. Mr. Dewey's principles of how to be a person are still worthy of our consideration. For example, he said:

What is the most hateful thing in the world now? It is this non-active but passive morality. Therefore, today's so-called good citizens are those sycophants who speak and act mediocrely, not those who have creative ability, a positive spirit, and a vigorous spirit to transform the world. Is this not a very hateful thing?

After reading this passage, I could not help but feel ashamed and deeply hate myself. As he also said:

Emotions can excite us, inspire us, and impel us. We cannot but follow them. Emotions such as hope, anger, joy, rage, love, and desire add so much color to life, so much fun and energy. Without them, how lifeless it would be! Even if there is reason, the ability to know and act, it is like a mechanical creation, a calculating machine, without joy in success or sorrow in failure, utterly boring. Therefore, life has interest and value because there are emotions. Otherwise, living is like being dead.

Currently, among our young people, there are many sycophants who are merely flattering the world and lack vitality. But we cannot help but hope that young friends will all be willing to "be those who have creative ability, a positive spirit, and a vigorous spirit to transform the world." Is Mr. Dewey's new moral doctrine not enough to be a kind of medicine for our youth? This is one of the reasons why I compiled this selection of speeches and put Mr. Dewey's two speeches at the end.

Dance Marathon (2)

— (Made by American L.I. Farael) Translated by Yi Xian

He also learned one thing, which was how to dance like an American. He had a friend who was a mixed Greek and American. This friend took him to a dance school called "Taxcance" on West Madison Street. He paid a dollar and got ten tickets, each ticket good for one to one and a half minutes of dancing. Every girl there was willing to dance with him, because she earned five cents for every minute. His tickets were used up quickly, and he bought some more. It didn't matter whether he could dance or not, the girls liked teaching him. He often went to dance halls, spending three, four, or five dollars each time. Occasionally, girls asked him if he would take her home, spending a few more dollars, and he could get some other benefits. Since he regularly went to dance halls, he was even less able to save money.

Once, Tax used his savings to buy a suit, with trousers that had wide legs. He kept his hair short, and put pomade on it, parting it in the middle. Only then did he look like a wealthy young man. He paid attention to all the words that American wealthy young men spoke. So he went to public dance halls, which only charged an entrance fee and allowed you to dance for a long time. There were often large groups of girls there, beautiful American girls, some with long, beautiful, milky skin and cherry-like red lips. He asked them to dance. They often danced with him once. But when he started to chat, they paid attention to his tone. If he asked them to dance again, they apologized and said that they had a date for the next dance. Therefore, when he danced there, he often had to dance with those showy, ugly girls who were called "wallflowers." So he went back to the dance halls, where it cost a dime to dance once, and all the girls were willing to dance with him.

One day, Tax turned twenty-five. His Greek mountain home was only a vague shadow in his memory. He had lived in America for twelve years. He worked ten hours a day in a bar, earning ten dollars a week, and secretly had three to five dollars of extra income each week. He wanted to get rich. He wanted to wait until he opened his own bar or restaurant, became rich, and took an American wife back to Greece to show off like a big boss. He had thirty-five dollars in the bank, which could be used as the foundation for making such a great fortune.

Loan

— Xu Ying

On the day the "Cotton Loan" certificates were issued, people were so busy from dawn to dusk that they didn't even have time to drink a cup of tea. Farmers from all directions were packed tightly around the primary school. It was bustling like a gathering.

I was surrounded by our own people, who exchanged the permits they had received for loan certificates under my hand. Farmers came in batches and went out in batches. They surrounded us, with a circle of temporary counters made of students' desks and chairs separating us.

Ever since I brushed my teeth outside the door, when the sky was slightly bright, the new moon hung in the sky, and there were still shadows on the ground, there were already farmers who had come early waiting quietly. After that, with the crowing of the rooster, people came like a tide. In addition to the three classrooms that had been converted into reception rooms, which were full, the small playground also seemed like a temple fair, with people squeezing against each other, craning their necks towards the certificate exchange point, and chattering noisily.

Both the "entrance" and the "exit" were full of people, making it difficult to get in and out. Although the self-defense corps members were clearing the way with sticks, it was still ineffective. Seeing that the order was about to become unmanageable, I asked someone with a loud voice to shout:

"Everyone, stop crowding. If you crowd again, we won't issue money slips today."

These words were powerful. No one had rushed here before dawn without the two-yuan-per-mu loan. For the sake of the money, their tense situation eased, and we opened up the entrance and exit, allowing people to come in one by one and go out one by one.

At the beginning of sunrise, my pen began to move non-stop, and I couldn't stop even when the clock struck twelve. For the sake of the dark crowd waiting quietly outside the window, my conscience did not allow me to rest. I could not make the members wait from morning until dark.

"..." The members quietly exchanged their certificates and went out.

My head was dizzier than being exposed to the scorching sun, my eyes were going black, and the words I wrote seemed to have legs. At the same time, my wrist was also a little sore. Among our group of responsible people, no one had yet expressed fatigue, and I didn't have the courage to suggest a rest.

The work continued for another hour. The staff alternated, but I was still writing.

"Jiaocun Sun Dade... two and a half mu of land,... only one and a half mu of cotton..."

Hearing the validator shout this, I suddenly felt a slight prick. I remembered three days ago, when a middle-aged woman came to my house and sent a gift, saying that she was asking me to give Sun Dade a helping hand on his behalf. After she finished speaking, she left the gift and left.

My spirits were restored. I stared at the thin, small man with a few withered, yellow rat whiskers outside the counter. The man's head was bowed.

"Are you Sun Dade?..."

"Uh...uh..." He seemed to know why I was paying special attention to him, but he also seemed a little embarrassed and couldn't speak.

"You can only get three yuan. Take your twenty eggs back and have your woman take them back - it's official business..." I said.

"Uh! Uh!"

I wrote the number "three" on a pre-printed voucher. This thin, honest man received the voucher and carefully put it in his arms and walked out, glancing back at me a little fearfully.

Bribery is just as common in the countryside...

This continued until dusk, and there were fewer and fewer people. I took the opportunity to go outside the door to order a meal. The teahouse on this small stall was full of people. Today was a very profitable day. The waiter said to me:

"Will you still be giving out loans tomorrow, sir!"

Morning Climb of Guānxiàng Mountain

— Liu Ming

—One of the Impressions of Qingdao—

Guānxiàng Mountain, with the observatory and some small pine trees, stands in the center of the city.

Once you climb up, countless red rooftops and Qingdao, surrounded by blue bays on three sides, are clearly revealed in the fresh morning sunlight, immediately giving one a completely European flavor.

The sea surface to the west, perhaps affected by the wind or due to the morning climate, showed two different colors: gray-blue and gray-white. The gray-white area blended with the horizon, merging into one. The brown sailboats sailing on it were simply like hanging in the air, evoking the fantasy of a mirage.

In the bay to the south, near the naval dock, a gray foreign warship appeared, like a tiger or wolf lying there, waiting to devour people.

The Westernized city, quietly lying at the foot of the mountain, was like a blessed Western young master, quietly enjoying the rest of the night's sleep.

The Jiaoji train, which had worked hard all night in the Shandong wilderness, was probably feeling dissatisfied with this, as it was still roaring and roaring along the seaside at the foot of the mountain to the north.

Next to the railway, the ships at the big and small ports, perhaps expressing sympathy, were also helping to cheer by shouting once or twice.

The Catholic Church, using the majestic posture of its twin towers, stood in the air as if to overwhelm all the buildings beneath its feet, as if trying to show its dignity and not be disturbed by anything.

However, the two tall chimneys standing far away next to the National Bridge, like hooligans outside a church door, opened their mouths with an air of contempt for everything and spewed mocking black smoke into the sky?

As the sun rose higher, the city sounds gradually became louder, and I slowly walked down the mountain.

Scenery

— Cun Yin

The internal scenery that cannot be hidden,

Fell from the solar system onto people's heads.

Withered, that trivial flower.

The soul expresses satisfaction.

There is a boat swaying on the coast that is difficult to dissolve.

There is gentle beauty underneath the secret,

If I could put on a golden dress,

Without time,

I will stand on her vermilion face.

Holding her in my arms and running hard,

Without time, without light.

She struggles desperately, I run desperately.

Not far from the prominent coastline,

She is sleeping delicately, and I have stopped.

Mountain Pastoral (2)

— Ai Wu

"Complaining, it doesn't matter, it doesn't cost anything!... It's always better for travelers to be amiable."

"Sitting in the shop doesn't count, acting big here, scaring crows? I just don't like complaining. People like that want to take up eight seats for eating and occupy the best beds at the inn. It's just a bit a bit..."

Old Chen hadn't found the right words when he heard Boss Qin sighing behind him, so he didn't say it.

"What kind of straw sandals are these? They're like they've grown mouths! Ugh, they're practically biting people..."

Old Xu heard Boss Qin's complaints and said to Old Chen:

"Forget it, listen, his feet must be blistered... If we don't let him rest, he'll realize it. We're all travelers, so it's better to be a little considerate. It's not worth offending people!"

"What? Can't you carry it anymore?" Old Chen turned around and asked coldly. "If you can't walk, then rest!"

"Where is it? What does this count for? I'm saying we should wait for him to get better. It's not worth..."

"Are you afraid of offending him? Just follow me, and I'll deal with him." Then Old Chen shouted loudly to Boss Qin: "Hey, Boss Qin, are your feet hurting? We can't rest on this section of mountain road, you know? Alas, it depends on everyone's luck today..."

Walking in the mountains where it is not easy to see people is difficult to do. Even if one knows that there is no danger, if someone suddenly mentions that one should be careful, then one cannot help but become timid. Because the mountain roads in the border areas of China are always unpredictable. Therefore, although Boss Qin replied with a suspicious tone, "I don't think so!", he unconsciously quickened his pace and no longer tried to come up with various ways to get everyone to rest.

Old Chen turned around and saw this short man limping along, and he continued walking while laughing happily to himself.

These three people had accidentally met on the road. Because of the loneliness and the habit of travelers chatting casually with strangers, they started by borrowing fire for their dry tobacco, one asking "May I ask your name?" and the other replying "I dare not, my surname is Chen." Then they began to talk about the weather, business, and the splendor of that hotel on a certain street. Thus, from the perspective of others, they seemed to be partners who had agreed to travel together. However, this requires that they are dressed similarly, and that the weight and value of each other's baggage are not too different; otherwise, they still cannot get along. The reason why Boss Qin and Old Chen were at odds was precisely because, comparatively, Boss Qin's clothes were too proper. Furthermore, after scrutinizing Old Chen and Old Xu deeply from head to toe with sharp eyes, he coldly replied to their greetings, and when Old Chen, with a cigarette holder in his mouth, asked him for fire, he only grunted from his nostrils and raised his dry tobacco pipe, as if he was extremely impatient.

Page 17

Shun Pao Local Supplement

Talk

Right to One's Name

— Ge

It is reported that lawyer Lai Yunhui, representing Ms. Yang Xiuqiong, issued a statement regarding the right to one's name, saying that it is proper for young people to study physical education and practice swimming, but it is inappropriate for someone to compile and print books using her name as a selling point, which violates Article 19 of the Civil Code regarding the right to one's name, and so on.

Yang Xiuqiong became famous for participating in the Far Eastern Games and was called the Mermaid. She was hired at a high price to perform in Nanchang. When she came to Shanghai, there were even incidents where she could not go into the water due to the crowd. She is a rare swimming talent in Chinese sports history.

However, after making one speech, she quietly returned to Guangzhou. At that time, some people said that being called "Mermaid" was an insult to women, and that these three words might ruin her future. In fact, the origin of "Mermaid" may not have been intentionally frivolous. However, Yang Xiuqiong is a "lady," so unfounded slanders arose when discussing her marriage.

Now, the statement in the newspaper says that the publisher is using her name as a selling point for compiling and printing books. Presumably, it is some kind of sports book, but the author has not seen it and does not know whether it is malicious or well-intentioned. Judging from the matter itself, the bookseller is using Yang Xiuqiong's name for business purposes. Moreover, I have not reviewed Article 19 of the Civil Code to see what the regulations on the right to one's name are. To what extent must the infringement reach before one can request the court to remove the infringement and obtain damages? I remember that a certain weaving factory used Ms. Yang's beautiful photo while swimming in an advertisement, boasting about how their swimwear was different from the crowd, as if Ms. Yang had even personally written the inscription: Although there is a difference between "agreeing" and "disagreeing," it is similar to "infringement," with little difference.

These are just random thoughts, and I am not blaming Ms. Yang for favoring one over the other, or perhaps the book that is now being used as a selling point is indeed something that makes people unable to restrain themselves from speaking out. However, going one step further, people in society today cannot "become famous." Slightly outstanding figures are soon seen as tools to be exploited. The advertisements of venereal disease doctors and wild chicken schools all drag in a large number of well-known figures. In the meantime, sending a mimeographed letter to seek consent is one in a hundred. (Whether they agree or not is naturally still a question.) When Ms. Yang returned to Guangdong, she said that she was "seeking further education." Even if people use this to promote themselves, as long as they do not intentionally "infringe," what does it matter? Publishing the advertisement might revive old cases and serve as conversation material for many people. Thinking of the dead who wrote "Human Words Are Terrifying" in a bloody suicide note, how their names were being "infringed" upon! Alas!

When Living in Indifference

— Xu Xizhen

I will never forget it: when there was a time when the uncontrollable express train of life, due to a moment of carelessness amongst a thousand cautions, rushed into the deserted wilderness, into the cold and endlessly long underground tunnel, then, from the past painful experiences, I knew: there would surely be a long, endless night without stars or moonlight waiting for me, and the weather ahead would be as cold as the severe ice of the North.

When the heavy night falls, I will not be able to see people, nor myself; a kind of terror and suspicion will never be forgotten, as familiar as returning to my old home, and without hesitation, will come to visit the tired heart that I have secretly hidden; and then, without any consideration, will continuously knock on it with cold sounds, like a snake, like lightning.

The result is: this unpleasant, shudder-inducing guest of thought, rudely snatches away one's heart. A kind of cold air passes through the whole body, reminding me of the great white bear galloping in the snowy lands of North America, rude and proud—yes, when life is not very easy, and this not very easy life falls into the terrible indifference of the human world, I feel that the world has abandoned me; and I, in the flames of anger, may think that I no longer need this world, and the indifference hidden within it.

Can it be said that the instinct for survival of living beings is itself a sin? Who can believe it? But the phenomenon of life vaguely reveals to us in the distance: "Strive to walk on the road to survival: the instinct for survival, even if it is not a sin, but every living thing endowed with the instinct for survival, must suffer the innocent punishment of the human world!"

It's all hard to bear! But everyone feels that the area traversed by life's express train has no beautiful scenery; on the contrary, the train is always stumbling and tumbling in windy and rainy weather. And the countless souls dwelling inside are just like prisoners exiled to a desolate area, undoubtedly forever whipped and punished by the whips of human indifference and treacherousness—only able to throw the good-hearted enthusiasm of the human world into the wind and rain outside without any consideration.

Perhaps someone in the cage might boldly stick their head out to take a look? But the scene is worrying: lying ahead is a winding, impossibly long, narrow road, and the fog is constantly thickening in the endless wind and rain; thus, people are filled with suspicion: "In the indifference of the outside world, perhaps ahead is the unknowable end of the world, the final reckoning of destruction?"

However, this is ultimately a mystery—a fog-like mystery!

(Who has ever thought of cursing the treacherousness of the human world? In a long string of difficult days, it is common to live a terrible and careless life: thus, along with the frightening waves of life, some rotten, abandoned waste and dregs flow along: human indifference, human treacherousness, human mutual framing and deception, human brown cunning!)

As if just waking up from a vague nightmare, past suffering has finally revealed to me something elusive: the indifference of the human world always stands like a stubborn iceberg in front of me, and it is not easy for people whose hands and feet are bound by life to climb over that thousand-foot cold cliff, because survival itself, it is said, is an unforgivable sin; and people must use the indifference they spit out to harm themselves.

Let's also praise this as the glory of mankind (if you don't want to say "shameful words"), when life falls into indifference!

Trip to Haiyan

— Li Sanlang

Luxuriant reeds grow on top of the loose yellow clay soil, and the azure sky reflects the lightness and calmness of the coast. The sound of the surging sea is always the same unchanging tune, shasha, bobo, giving people the feeling that this calm coast is somewhat empty and sad. Looking from the fiery wheel tossing on the sea surface, you can clearly see the winding coastline unfolding far away. The sound of the rocks on the shore being struck by the waves and echoing, and the silvery white spray, are the same from afar, a kind of faint sorrow.

With the wandering melancholic steps of a vagabond, I jumped out of the city and quietly drifted to the coastal village following the tide of the surging sea. — It seems that my fate is carved as a wandering, suffering person. From childhood to youth, I have lived an unstable life without rest. However, anyway, I hope to find the miracle I yearn for on that dark journey. Yes! In that unhypocritical city, with the same terrible, ferocious faces and the cruel, plundering whips in the countryside, especially on the coast still carrying the breath of the primitive—I am so eager to find the happiness of the human world that I think of in such a place. But is this a dream? When things give me a more realistic and clear understanding, I feel that not only the quiet countryside has been ravaged as coldly and sadly by the same evildoers as the modern city, but also the remote, tranquil coast, still carrying the breath of the primitive, has clearly revealed that the storm of the times has swept everywhere—Oh, am I fantasizing? — Young people without much experience are always enthusiastic and yearning. However, when a disappointment and a cold draft are given in reality, they will always think that the whips of the evil of the times possess everything in this society.

Leaving the sea-going life, my two legs straddled Haiyan Street, a small town of the eighteenth century and also a vast village. From the small boats floating in the creek surrounding the reeds, you can see that it stands like a Hong Kong-style island, with high peaks with buildings that are neither new nor old, and tower-like碉樓(diaolou, watchtowers), and a simple shadow penetrates the traveler's heart. I pray to get my experience in such a coastal town, and get the original form of everything in human question.

Page 18

At first, I wandered with my friends among all the unique scenery. I did not forget that the part I needed was a quiet and beautiful landscape. It was early spring at that time, and the gentle wind drifting from the distant Indian Ocean to the South China Sea was rippling like bewitching the hearts of travelers. The sea breeze seems to have no peculiar atmosphere at all, only feeling the beauty and horror of spring. However, I stepped over the green mountains and swayed through the green sea, but still could not find what I longed to desire. Only what I saw was the traces of the war hidden many years ago—like sad arrows, passing over my heart, so faint and desolate.

Before long, when I felt that Haiyan was so boring and had stepped into the circle of the sorrow of the times, I began to drift to other places on the sea again, still so quietly!

Celebrated Person in the Countryside

— Erlang

"Are you talking about Xihe Xian? I know him, I know him, we're acquainted."

The visitor shouted loudly, and then recounted Xihe Xian's recent situation as if telling a story.

"In our town, Xihe Xian is the most humorous and a learned man. Although he is a doctor, he is a 'halfway monk' Confucian doctor. In the past, I heard that he was also a Xiucai [successful candidate in the imperial examinations]. A Xiucai is already enough to be respected in our town, let alone this Xiucai is also learned? The doctor is learned and also a Xiucai, so Xihe Xian is regarded as a sage by the people of the town. When he goes out to make house calls, people greet him on the road. Some call out, 'Where are you going, Xiucai?' Some call out, 'Are you going to see a patient, doctor?' They are all expressing their respect for him. He is also very amiable. To those who greet him, whether they are old people or women, he always answers with a smile, 'Going to see a patient.' or 'Yes, going to see a patient.' However, when he passes by the tavern, the old tavern owner always winks at him and secretly asks him with gestures: 'Have a drink?' Then he opens his mouth and says, 'Have a drink and then go, it doesn't matter, the money will be recorded on the signboard.' Because Xihe Xian always says, 'I didn't bring any money' when he encounters the tavern owner's greeting.

"Xihe Xian! That's what we young people call him! Since he likes to have a drink or two, it's no wonder the tavern owner wants to solicit his business, but Xihe Xian is not a person who can drink, only drinks a cup or two, and the face with a large head and a sharp chin, like a gourd, turns red, wipes his mouth with his sleeve, and says, 'I'm drunk, I'm drunk'! Sometimes he just leaves like that. Sometimes he doesn't want to leave, but starts chatting in the tavern. He is a learned man, and apart from the tavern owner, no one is qualified to talk to him. He is also a learned man. I heard that he can recite the entire 'Romance of the Three Kingdoms' from beginning to end, it's really amazing. When two learned men meet, they inevitably argue. Once, they even fell out over the question of whether Cao Cao in the Romance of the Three Kingdoms was a bad guy; Xihe Xian didn't go to the tavern to drink for several days, and the tavern owner didn't greet him to have a drink either. At that time, Xihe Xian was arguing that Cao Cao was an amazing figure, while the tavern owner was arguing that Cao Cao was a big villain. At first, they argued according to reason, but later, Xihe Xian opened his eyes and stretched his finger fiercely to the tavern owner's nose and shouted, 'You know shit, Cao Cao can write poetry, can Liu Bei write poetry?' The tavern owner also didn't show weakness and slapped the table and said, 'Cao Cao is a treacherous hero, Liu Bei is a benevolent lord, what's the use of being able to write poetry, why didn't Kongming join Cao Cao but joined Liu Bei? Xihe Xian thought for a while, he couldn't win the argument with reason, he was ashamed into anger, and shouted angrily, 'You know shit, you know shit'! The tavern owner was also angered by being scolded, and said, 'You only know shit, you only know shit'! The two fell out like that. Xihe Xian seemed to have broken off relations with the tavern owner for several days.

"Now his beard is white, and the tavern owner has already died. Although he still goes to the tavern to drink as usual, no one argues with him anymore."

Alley

— Rong

From dawn, this alley is filled with noisy sounds. The shouting of vegetable sellers, the playing of children, the senseless quarrels of neighbors, the bicycle bell of the newspaper delivery man, all mixed together to form a hubbub in the air. If it is at lunchtime, all sounds become even more noisy. Even in the dead of night, you can often hear the footsteps of night travelers, the sound of knocking on doors. This alley plays that annoying and vulgar music all day and all night. And I am deeply annoyed by this music.

In my annoyance, the impressions of two alleys came into my consciousness.

The first alley was in Beiping, a nostalgic place where I lived for several years. The alley I lived in was a long one. The vermilion gates of each house and the verdant trees at the entrance formed an extremely beautiful contrast. In spring, the alley was full of falling locust flowers. Some blackbirds came to peck at the leaves on the treetops. Everything was filled with such a medieval air of tranquility. It's not that there were no peddlers, but their cries were like a piece of court music. Early morning almond tea, late-night hard noodles, iced drinks in summer, sweet grapes and dates in early autumn, even a barber's burden, a junk collector, their voices were gentle and full of poetry. Early in the morning, a snail-like water cart passed through the alley, leaving people with the water they needed. Sometimes some carriages and horses passed by, but by dusk it was completely quiet. Then we could linger in the courtyard, enjoying those priceless moments of happiness, watching the horns slowly fall, watching the black crows returning to their nests flying all over the sky, watching the bats, and night came unnoticed. Passing the day like this, even sleeping at night was comfortable, and dreams were light.

I can't forget that alley, I can't forget that alley!

Another alley. In Suzhou, a city overflowing with poetry, embracing the name of paradise, there was an alley where I once lived. Although it didn't have much of the flavor of a waterside town, its tranquility still attracts my dreams to this day. Planted with trees, the alley was full of green shade. Half of the stone slabs underfoot were moist. Shut inside the door, you never heard a bit of noise, except for the sound of the wind blowing through the leaves whispering, and the sound of people coming from the opposite courtyard. Peaches, pomegranates, and balsam were planted in the courtyard. Everything was like the "daytime scene" chanted in ancient poetry. During the day, you could hear rickshaws dragging past outside the door, and low calls of peddlers. By dusk, everything was as if bewitched and became quiet. Then we could hear the neighbors putting up the door panels and window panels, hear the sound of a fortune teller walking in the dark alley knocking on a small copper gong, and hear the sound of an old lay Buddhist in the house behind chanting scriptures while striking a clear chime and wooden fish. Slowly all these disappeared, and what was placed in front of us was a long, gentle, and lovely black robe. And we also sank into sleep.

Then, on the second day, it would come again like this, familiar, but not monotonous. I love that alley, and I love the people in that alley and their lives even more!

These two poetic alleys that were related to my life often visit my imagination when I am upset. I can't live through these noisy days. In the city, I once visited all sides to find similar alleys, but all I got was disappointment. Near Jing'an Temple Road, there is one called Lovw Lane. The name is very charming, quiet, with window screens that let through the light, and the sound of piano flowing from the other side. The shadows of the trees swayed slowly under the streetlights, but that was always too "metropolitan" and too "modern". So I didn't make a second visit to that place.

I just miss those two alleys, and it's a kind of half-melancholy and half-sweet nostalgia!

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Excerpt from "Leimen Noveluo Leaves MGM"

— Wen Ying

Of the many male stars in Hollywood that we enjoy watching, even if Leimen Noveluo cannot be considered the absolute top, he can certainly be ranked among the best. Therefore, any news concerning him, especially rumors that he is leaving the silver screen, is something that everyone is eager to know about.

Is Leimen Noveluo really not making any more films? Have his fame and his struggle for fame shattered his silver dreams? What are his future plans? How is he living now? These are all questions we want answered.

He has been a star in Hollywood for thirteen consecutive years. He is a handsome young man, a silver screen idol worshipped by millions. Idealists around the world regard him as the epitome of male perfection. But recently, something seems to have gone wrong. His box office earnings have gradually declined, and his films have lacked the captivating magic. Most recently, at the beginning of this year, he suddenly announced his departure from MGM, his long-time employer of over a decade. At the time, after filming "The Night Is Young," MGM was planning to shoot another grand musical film. However, Leimen requested that the company release him from his duties. The company, seeing his sincere plea, had no choice but to agree. Thus, he left the silver film circle. But as a result, rumors have flourished.

Recently, a journalist, being an old friend of Leimen, made a special trip to his house to interview him and ask him what was really going on. But Leimen Noveluo replied without hesitation, "What? Leave the movies? Of course not. If I have any sense, I certainly wouldn't. I wouldn't stop working either. Lost my ambition? A person who loses their ambition is half-dead. But... in the immediate future, I don't want to make any more films, because the stories in the films I've been making lately really bore me. I feel like my film career has a major problem. Do you know what it is? It's a lack of progress. For years, I haven't made any progress. In the last five years, I haven't done anything I should have done."

Indeed, Leimen Noveluo's words are both honest and insightful. He is not one to deceive himself. He continued, "A person's art should also improve with age. I am an adult now. I don't want to live in the past forever. I don't want to keep playing the same stories over and over again. Viennese romances, football stories... My departure from MGM was amicable, but that's the reason. What's the point of repeating the same themes over and over?"

Under the constraints of his contract, Leimen Noveluo did not have the freedom to choose his own stories, so he had to temporarily announce his departure. He said, "I no longer feel any interest in the issues of ten years ago. Although with my looks, I can still play characters younger than my actual age, my state of mind is no longer that of ten years ago. In 'The Night Is Young,' I played a 25-year-old young man, but in my best efforts, all I could do was imitate my past performances. Therefore, I asked myself: 'Is this sustainable?'"

"Even doing that is not an easy task. Constantly playing the role of a romantic lead, always trying to give people something different to see, is extremely difficult. It would be different if I were a woman, because, you know, actresses can constantly change their outfits, hairstyles, and makeup. But a man..." As he said this, he smiled mischievously and winked.

Leimen is now writing a play called "Another Story." It tells the story of a movie star who, after being a star for over ten years, becomes tired of it and is willing to sacrifice his star status and income to go on stage. This is likely Leimen Noveluo's own "confession," as he is seriously considering going to London to perform on stage and temporarily change his surroundings.

Film Review

Review of "Sweet Adeline"

— Chan Fei

Sweet Adeline – Cathay Film

If one were to argue that musical films do not require substantial content and only need to be visually stunning, then "Sweet Adeline" would be praised. This is Warner Bros.'s big musical film following "42nd Street," "Footlight Parade," "Gold Diggers of 1933," and "Dames." However, judging solely on form while disregarding content is not a reasonable argument. No matter how brilliantly the form expresses its golden and dazzling aspects, the impact it has on the audience will ultimately be infinitely empty.

"Sweet Adeline" also fails to escape the old cliché of unprincipled romantic love, a cliché that has already made people feel bored and weary. What is never lacking here is intoxicating jazz music, extravagant and decadent dances, the gimmicks of comical characters, and passionate embraces and kisses. All these things, considered essential for old-fashioned musical films, are all present in "Sweet Adeline." However, due to the shallowness and vulgarity of the content, all this extravagance and decadence is nothing more than a technically proficient accumulation of artists trying to mask emptiness. Who can discern any meaning of life or reflection of the times in this? It is proving to be quite difficult for new types of musical films to emerge in America.

Yes, this film naturally cannot satisfy those who seek realistic portrayals, but for soft gentlemen who crave wild enjoyment, it is intoxicating liquor. For example, the wildly joyous chorus in the hotel, the dances reflected in the mirror, and the love songs on the swing frame under the brilliant starlight and flowing water of the lawn… all cater lavishly to the tastes of gentlemen and ladies. Who can deny that these are not the peak expressions of American musical films? It is truly an intoxicating film, but also an empty film that obscures the true meaning of life.

That's all I want to say about the film itself. Because this film is Mervyn Leroy's, the director of "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang," work following "Footlight Parade," I want to say something about him. Chinese audiences, at the same time, had high expectations for him after "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang" left a deep impression.

Generally speaking, film directors, like artists in other fields, have their own worldviews and distinct styles. In America, we can name at least a few, such as Frank Borzage's sentimentalism, which is consistently expressed from "Seventh Heaven" to "Man's Castle." King Vidor expresses a consistent humanism and reformism in works such as "The Crowd" and "Our Daily Bread." Cecil B. DeMille appears as a religious author with a penchant for historical dramas. Ernst Lubitsch maintains a consistent fantasy and lightness in "The Love Parade" or "The Merry Widow." All of them consistently maintain their inherent styles. But Mervyn Leroy is similar to Rouben Mamoulian. Mamoulian produced the legendary "Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde" and the love-supremacy "Song of Songs" or "Queen Christina." Mervyn Leroy produced the cutting-edge, reality-exposing "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang" and the content-lacking musical "Footlight Parade" or "Sweet Adeline," and even vulgar works like "The World Changes." Taking "Footlight Parade" as an example, it at least included a scene of unemployed veterans seeking relief, touching on reality to some extent. "Sweet Adeline" does not even achieve this much. Of course, this is limited by the script, but the fact that he does not have a fixed style and that his works do not express his own worldview is very obvious.

With this in mind, people do not need to have overly high expectations for him. Moreover, considering that he was able to become the son-in-law of Warner Bros. boss Jack Warner, perhaps he is just a commercial writer who prioritizes business above all else.

Clark Gable and Constance Bennett's first collaboration in "Night Flight" (originally translated as "Amateur Reporter") – Nanjing Showing

This supplement is a film publication dedicated to promoting culture and art. We welcome external submissions and offer generous compensation upon publication.

Once a written piece is published and compensated, the copyright belongs to Shen Bao.

The language of this publication is primarily modern vernacular Chinese, and new-style punctuation must be used.

Each submission must include a seal; otherwise, it will not be compensated.

Due to limited space, articles should be concise, ideally around 500 characters in length.

Translated works must include the original text. Avoid excessive use of English where possible.

Unless otherwise stated in advance with a return address and postage, we are not responsible for preserving or returning written pieces, photos, etc.

Do not write on both sides of the paper, write horizontally, or use pencils.

Submissions that are simultaneously submitted to other publications, plagiarized, or directly copied from explanatory materials will not be compensated upon detection.

Film Novel

Clouds, Sky, and Hate (Living on Velvet) (3)

— Ti Yun

Tuoguan raised his head, looked up at the sky, and said thoughtfully, "I don't know myself either. There might be something in there... that wanted my life but didn't succeed. I just want to give it another chance." Soon, they arrived at Huade's house. Tuolei was shaving, and Huade was standing beside him talking to him. Tuolei suddenly stopped, raised his razor, and asked Huade, "Why are you telling me to shave?" Huade said, "We're going to a party."

Tuolei said, "Whose party?" Huade said, "Aimei Boluntisi's party. She lives with her aunt, Masha Boluntisi. Her aunt might not approve of your behavior." Tuolei asked again, "Who is Aimei Boluntisi?" Huade hesitated for a moment, then said, "She might marry me. I love her deeply, but she... doesn't love me quite as much." Tuolei, while lathering, continued to ask, "What kind of person is she?" Huade said seriously, "About forty-five years old... weighs a little over two hundred pounds... her eyes are blue... I mean one of them... her skin is speckled." Tuolei interjected, "In short, the best there is." Huade said, "That's right. She is beautiful, lovely, polite, and very intelligent..." They finished speaking and laughed at each other.

In the evening, Huade took Tuolei to Aimei Boluntisi's house. Tuolei felt that everyone was staring at him because everyone had read the evening newspaper, and most of the newspaper's account of the air force exercise described this arrogant, uninvited guest. But Tuolei didn't feel uncomfortable at all. Later, he met a girl with dark hair and fair skin, and he cared even less about people's attention.

Tuolei didn't know who the girl was. The two of them seemed to have met by chance and began dancing unconsciously. He found her perfume lovely, as well as her pout and her throaty voice with its slight awkwardness. He didn't even think that this girl might be Aimei. He completely forgot what Huade had told him that afternoon. All he knew was that the woman he was holding in his arms now was the most perfect woman he had ever seen in his life. He didn't care who she was. He didn't have time to ask her.

As for Aimei—because it was indeed Aimei—she was temporarily seduced by his rough and aloof attitude. When the music stopped, the two of them were at the entrance to the lawn. Unconsciously, Tuolei led her out. Strangely, they seemed like old friends, not needing to ask each other's names and not even needing to talk. Aimei kept listening to his laughter. What he said was not important or consistent, but his eyes contained profound meaning. Tuolei suddenly asked, "How about we leave here?" Aimei quickly said, "Oh, no, no, the guests are just arriving one by one." Tuolei said, "I know, but... please..." Aimei seemed to have lost consciousness. She was caught off guard, and by the time she realized it, the two of them were already sitting on a bus. (To be continued)
