Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

Key Points of the Latest Hospital Architectural Designs (Part 1)

— Liu Ji Piao

The responsibility of establishing a hospital lies in helping the world and saving lives. In this era of advancing culture, building hospitals is an essential task. However, hospital architecture is truly a place for the implementation of science and applied technology. All plans are more complex than other buildings. Therefore, designers should first have knowledge of hospital equipment. At the same time, they must have detailed discussions with experienced hospital administrators before proceeding. Otherwise, they will be like blind men leading blind horses, unable to start. The following are the key points in the latest hospital designs, briefly described as follows.

(1) Bed Allocation: Beds are provided to meet the needs of patients. Those wishing to build a hospital must predetermine the number of beds. However, the situation varies from place to place, and needs also differ accordingly. Generally speaking, based on statistics from prosperous cities, there should be one internal medicine/surgical bed, one infectious disease bed, one pediatric bed, and one obstetrical bed for every 2,000 residents. However, this ratio is subject to change for four reasons: (1) Epidemic outbreaks; (2) Different social situations; (3) Different population growth rates; (4) The number of hospitals. Therefore, to make accurate statistics, a detailed investigation must be conducted first.

(2) Site Selection: The most important aspect is site selection. If the location is appropriate, everything is easier to solve. Therefore, attention should be paid to several factors when selecting a site:

A (Quiet): It should be away from railroads, factories, busy streets, and public gathering places such as churches, schools, sports fields, and markets.

B (Fresh Air): It should avoid places with smoke and foul odors, such as manufacturing plants, train stations, and unpaved main roads.

C (Few Insects): It should be away from stables, warehouses, ponds, and wet, dirty areas.

D (Suitable Scenery): The scenery should be quiet and not noisy, elegant and pleasant, so that patients can relax their minds. Therefore, fields, forests, and distant mountains are suitable as natural scenery.

E (Sunlight Orientation): A site should be selected that allows the arrangement of patient rooms to receive at least some sunlight every day.

F (Permanence): Avoid areas that could become commercial or industrial centers in the future.

G (Future Expansion): The rate of future development is unpredictable. Land should be prepared for expansion to twice the current size.

H (Convenient Transportation): Although the above mentions being away from commercial and industrial centers, it should not be too remote. Otherwise, the transportation of patients and supplies will be difficult.

(3) Arrangement of Various Sections

A (Administration Department): This is the head of the entire plan. The plan should include a warm welcome, close friendship, and sincere hospitality to increase its development power.

1. Entrance Hall: Should include an information desk, public telephone, reception room, public restrooms, etc.

2. Offices: General office, individual offices, meeting rooms, etc.

3. Business Office: Patient registration room, maternity monitoring room, medical guidance room, etc.

4. Social Services Department: Staff offices, library, emergency room, patient transport entrance, examination room, etc.

B (Public Area): The public area's stairs, corridors, etc., should be located in the center of the building for easy access.

1. Corridors: Corridors leading to public and private patient rooms should be at least eight feet wide. This width allows two beds to pass side by side. If the corridor is longer, the width should also be increased. Patients, visitors, doctors, and nurses must all pass through the corridors. In each floor's corridor, there should be a small room of 6 feet x 7 feet for pushing in beds. Natural light and ventilation are important requirements in the corridors and should be considered.

2. Stairs: Must be located in the central part for easy access. There should be at least two for sufficient use. The width of the stairs cannot be less than four feet. Wall-mounted handrails should be installed. The height of each step should be less than 7 inches, and the width should not be less than 10 inches.

3. Elevators: Used to transport patients from patient rooms to the operating room. The size should be based on accommodating the bed, nurses, and elevator operator. Therefore, 6 feet x 8 inches is suitable. There should be a space in front of the elevator. The walls should be made of wood strips and lime, so that the mechanical sound does not transmit to the corridor and enter the patient rooms. It can also be used as a waiting area to avoid congestion in the corridor.

Recent Building Situation in Hangzhou City

— Yang Dehui

Everyone knows that Hangzhou City is the provincial capital of Zhejiang Province and a historical city in our country. How is the construction industry doing within the city's area of 23.2 li in length and 36 li in width? I think everyone is eager to know! Now, let me report to you the recent building situation in Hangzhou City!

The rise and fall of a city depends on its population. Due to the increasing population of Hangzhou City over the years, the construction of residential buildings has developed more rapidly than other industries. Let's not compare the population of Hangzhou City in ancient times, but even compared to the population after the Revolutionary Army established Zhejiang Province, it will surprise us. According to the survey in October of the 16th year of the Republic [1927], the city's population was only 380,031. In the 17th year [1928], it was 451,147. In the 18th year [1929], it was 474,228. In the 19th year [1930], it increased to 506,930. In the 20th year [1931], it was 523,569. In the 21st year [1932], it decreased slightly to 522,529. In the 22nd year [1933], it increased again to 529,163. And according to the survey in September of last year, the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], it has reached 546,434. With such rapid population growth in these eight years, it is clear that the construction industry has flourished. Therefore, the increase in population and the need for construction in Hangzhou City are inevitable facts.

In the 22nd year of the Republic [1933], the construction of houses in Hangzhou City included 461 ordinary residential buildings, covering an area of 87,760.00 square meters, with a value of 1,068,830.00 yuan; 271 stores, covering an area of 33,120.00 square meters, with a value of 536,420.00 yuan; 56 factory buildings, covering an area of 13,280.00 square meters, with a value of 135,950.00 yuan; 5 public buildings, covering an area of 670.00 square meters, with a value of 18,000.00 yuan; 6 schools, covering an area of 2,140.00 square meters, with a value of 20,000.00 yuan; 1 entertainment venue, covering an area of 10.00 square meters, with a value of 400.00 yuan; and 65 other buildings, covering an area of 6,930.00 square meters, with a value of 119,670.00 yuan. The total construction area reached 141,770.00 square meters, with a total construction value of 1,396,493.00 yuan. And last year, according to the city government's report, from January to October, the construction area reached 140,460 square meters, with a total construction value of 1,795,500 yuan. A total of 782 permits were issued, an increase of about 400,000 yuan compared to the previous year. The report on classified construction only includes figures from January to June, including 297 ordinary residential buildings, covering an area of 55,730.00 square meters, with a value of 55,760.00 yuan; 121 stores, covering an area of 28,103.00 square meters, with a value of 217,770.00 yuan; 17 factory buildings, covering an area of 6,650.00 square meters, with a value of 76,550.00 yuan; 2 public buildings, covering an area of 460.00 square meters, with a value of 6,700.00 yuan; 4 schools, covering an area of 3,120.00 square meters, with a value of 92,700.00 yuan; and 40 other buildings, covering an area of *940.00 square meters, with a value of 81,670.00 yuan. If we compare it with the first half of the 22nd year, the construction in the first half of last year did not show any decline or reduction. This is due to the rapid increase in population, the renovation of various administrative and commercial institutions, and large-scale construction. At the same time, modern buildings tend to be luxurious, and the increase in construction value is naturally greater than before. Looking at the amount of house tax collected by the municipal government, it has only increased year after year without any significant decline. The income from house tax in the 16th year was 98,895.46 yuan, in the 17th year it was 398,703.53 yuan, in the 18th year it was 443,007.72 yuan, in the 19th year it was 497,593.36 yuan, in the 20th year it was 473,262.81 yuan, and in the 21st year it was 474,659.47 yuan. Last year, from January to October of the 23rd year, the income decreased significantly to only 188,337.115 yuan. However, this is not due to a decrease in population or a decline in construction, but rather due to the sluggish market and the withering of various industries and commerce, resulting in closures and suspensions of business. This has affected the income from house tax, leading to a decrease. According to the statistics of the city treasury's income, it accounts for 39.63%, ranking first!

At the same time, we can also see that the Bureau of Public Works built new roads from January to October of last year, including Shita'er Road, Qingtai Road, Xizhao Road, Guohuo Road, Sudi Roundabout, Xuxi Road, Maolong Road, Jiuxi Shibajian Road, Siyan Road, and Shuixi Road, completing a total of 26,827 square meters of road surface. These new roads facilitate transportation, which is a fact. However, the development of the construction industry is one of the main reasons for the construction of new roads! As mentioned above, the rise and fall of a city is based on its population, and the increase in population promotes the development of the construction industry. Therefore, the fact that the construction value of Hangzhou City increased last year compared to the previous year is a good sign. Facts tell us that the forward development of construction under the current trend has many evidences, and the construction of Hangzhou City is just one example.

Secondly, we also need to know about real estate, which is closely related to the construction industry. In the past, the land price per mu in the Shuishui Bridge, Qinghefang, Yangbatou, and Sanyuanfang areas of Hangzhou City's commercial center was generally 3,000 to 4,000 yuan. Now, due to the development of the construction industry, it has soared by 80% to 90%. According to recent estimates, the price per mu in Shuishui Bridge is 30,000 yuan, and in Qinghefang and Yangbatou it is about 20,000 yuan. Even in Zhongqing Street and Jianqiao Street, the center of the lower city, the land price per mu is about 10,000 yuan. As for the land price in the urban area, the highest price per mu in the Xinmin Road area was more than 2,000 yuan in the 12th year of the Republic [1923], but now it is 7,000 to 8,000 or even 10,000 yuan. The land price outside the urban area has also risen as high as in the urban area and the commercial center. Now, the municipal government is actively building roads and improving facilities, with the aim of prospering Hangzhou City. Therefore, the future value of real estate is just beginning to flourish, and it may soon rise again.

Psychological Design of Factory Buildings (Part 2)

— Bo Ning

As for the distance between factories, the most important thing is to be economical. If the distance is too far, the workers will waste too much unnecessary energy going back and forth.

2. Reserve sufficient open space for workers to rest: Fatigue is the venomous snake of work, which can reduce work efficiency to the minimum. Therefore, enlightened factories in Europe and America allow workers to have short breaks in the factory, ranging from three to five minutes.

However, the most important condition for rest is to get away from the workplace, so that their eyes are refreshed and their minds are open, making it easier to restore fresh energy. I often see that when workers in Chinese factories take breaks, they still stay in the factory, which is very psychologically inappropriate.

However, in cities, land prices are too high and spacious open spaces are hard to come by. Then, when designing, wider corridors or aisles should be left outside the factory for workers to rest.

(3) Internal Equipment: Once the external outline has been completely determined, the internal equipment must be discussed:

1. Lighting: Psychologists have done many experiments on lighting, and we can briefly describe their results:

The light coming in from windows and skylights should not be directly facing the workers' eyes, as this is enough to distract them. The color of the walls should be light yellow and not too smooth, so as to avoid reflection. The lighting at night is best built into dark lines. If this is not possible, then the light bulbs should be milky white and not shine directly on the workers' eyelids.

2. Noise Avoidance: The noisy sounds emitted by machines are most disturbing to the workers' minds, easily making them tired and weakening their nerves. This is the most uneconomical thing in work! When building, efforts should be made to reduce disturbing noises in the room to a minimum, which is really a meritorious act.

3. Ventilation: According to the research of the New York Ventilation Association: in public places with many people, the air exhaled from the mouth and the heat radiated from the body can increase the indoor temperature as much as possible, which can make people tired, sleepy, headache, and irritable. This is of course even worse in the factory. Because in addition to the heat generated by the workers themselves, there is also the heat generated by the machines, so the ventilation equipment in the factory is really urgent?

The above points, although very brief, although very superficial, are very important. If those who build factories can pay attention to them one by one, the welfare of the workers will certainly increase, and the benefits of the factory owners will certainly be very great.
